10:137:9795:0:40:90:219:560:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:Foreword
10:138:9803:40:15:90:504:520:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The Government has begun a major programme of pension reform. These reforms
10:139:9878:15:22:90:472:505:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:are based on an extensive, sound evidence base, contained, for example, in:
10:140:9953:22:22:90:332:483:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The First Report of the Pensions Commission;
10:141:10000:22:23:90:349:461:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The Second Report of the Pensions Commission;
10:142:10048:23:15:90:504:438:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•Security in Retirement: towards a new pensions system and its accompanying
10:143:10123:15:22:102:261:423:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Regulatory Impact Assessment;
10:144:10152:22:25:90:454:401:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The Pensions Bill and the accompanying documents published today.
10:145:10220:25:15:90:504:376:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Because of the scale and importance of these reforms, the Government is keen to
10:146:10299:15:15:90:504:361:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:continue to develop this evidence base. To contribute to this aim, the Government
10:147:10380:15:15:90:504:346:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:has undertaken, and continues to undertake, a range of innovative, exploratory
10:148:10458:15:15:90:504:331:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:analysis. This paper contains an exploration of method and early results from work
10:149:10540:15:15:90:504:316:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which examines the macro-economic and social welfare impacts of elements of
10:150:10615:15:25:90:128:301:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reform.
10:151:10622:25:15:90:504:276:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The analysis presented here is meant not as the conclusion of the work, but as an
10:152:10703:15:15:90:504:261:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:exposition of preliminary thinking. The Government would welcome the views of
10:153:10780:15:15:90:504:246:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:academics  and  other  experts  on  the  techniques  used  and  preliminary  findings
10:154:10865:15:15:90:504:231:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:presented.  Comments  should  be  directed  to  Clement  van  de  Coevering
10:155:10940:15:0:90:327:216:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:(Clement.Van-de-Coevering@dwp.gsi.gov.uk).
12:156:10990:0:40:90:218:561:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:Summary
12:157:10997:40:15:90:504:521:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This paper examines the impact of two effects of the pension reform package that
12:158:11077:15:15:90:504:506:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f9:was put forward in the May White Paper Security in retirement: towards a new
12:159:11153:15:15:90:504:491:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:pensions system: the likely increase in the number of older people working due to a
12:160:11236:15:15:90:504:476:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:higher State Pension age and the likely rise in saving due to more people putting
12:161:11317:15:25:90:230:461:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:away money for retirement.
12:162:11343:25:15:90:504:436:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State Pension age is currently 65 for men and 60 for women. There has been a long-
12:163:11425:15:15:90:504:421:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:planned increase in women’s pension age to 65, due to take place between 2010
12:164:11502:15:15:90:504:406:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and  2020,  which  is  not  examined  in  this  paper.  However,  the  Government  has
12:165:11588:15:15:90:504:391:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:announced that State Pension age for men and women will then rise from 65 to 66
12:166:11667:15:15:90:504:376:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:by 2026, to 67 by 2036 and to 68 by 2046. Not everyone retires at State Pension age,
12:167:11751:15:15:90:504:361:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:but it is likely that this increase will lead to more people working.  This will result in an
12:168:11844:15:15:90:504:346:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increase in the size of the economy. There is considerable uncertainty about people’s
12:169:11929:15:15:90:504:331:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:exact response to the reforms, so we present results as ranges. The paper explores
12:170:12011:15:15:90:504:316:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different techniques to estimate the size of this impact. It finds that by 2050 the
12:171:12094:15:15:90:504:301:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economy could be 1.4 – 1.7 per cent larger than it would be if reform had not taken
12:172:12177:15:25:90:120:286:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:place.
12:173:12183:25:15:90:504:261:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The introduction of personal accounts is thought likely to increase pension saving,
12:174:12266:15:15:90:504:246:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:although, again, individual responses are difficult to predict with certainty. Analysis
12:175:12353:15:15:90:504:231:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:suggests that the increase in saving for retirement could lead to a long-term growth
12:176:12437:15:15:90:504:216:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in UK incomes of around 0.2 per cent. This would occur as UK residents increased
12:177:12517:15:15:90:504:201:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their ownership of domestic and foreign companies and other assets that they invest
12:178:12600:15:15:90:504:186:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in  through  their  pension  funds.  The  ownership  of  these  assets  would  generate
12:179:12687:15:25:90:443:171:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:returns which would ultimately allow people in the UK to spend more.
12:180:12755:25:15:90:504:146:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The overall effect of changes to State Pension age and the introduction of personal
12:181:12838:15:15:90:504:131:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts on UK incomes is likely to be in the range of 0.9 – 3.1 per cent. Although
12:182:12921:15:15:90:504:116:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:these numbers are relatively small proportions of the total economy, they represent
12:183:13004:15:15:90:504:101:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:significant sums. In terms of today’s economy, they would be worth around £11 –
12:184:13083:15:0:90:140:86:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:38 billion.
13:185:13094:0:106:19:26:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:4
13:186:13095:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In addition to the economic impact of reform, the paper also explores its impact on
13:187:13178:15:25:90:410:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people’s wellbeing through improved consumption smoothing.
13:188:13236:25:15:90:504:675:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The Government provides a safety net to avoid pensioner poverty, and most people
13:189:13316:15:15:90:504:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:will achieve a basic level of pension through the State Pension system. However, it is
13:190:13402:15:15:90:504:645:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in most people’s interest to save on top of this for their retirement to avoid a big fall
13:191:13491:15:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in their income when they stop working. This is because many people prefer to
13:192:13568:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:maintain a reasonably smooth pattern of consumption throughout life, than to have
13:193:13649:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a relatively high level of consumption while they are working and then a much lower
13:194:13732:15:25:90:197:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:level once they retire.
13:195:13755:25:15:90:504:560:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Whilst  many  people  would  recognise  the  desirability  of  saving  for  retirement,
13:196:13842:15:15:90:504:545:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:analysis, for example presented by the Pensions Commission, suggests many are not
13:197:13923:15:15:90:504:530:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saving enough to smooth their consumption effectively. According to the latest
13:198:14001:15:15:90:504:515:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimates at least seven million people are currently not saving enough to avoid a
13:199:14083:15:15:90:504:500:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:significant fall in their standard of living at retirement. The introduction of personal
13:200:14171:15:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts is expected to lead to a large increase in the number of people saving for
13:201:14254:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their retirement, leading them to be able to maintain a more consistent standard of
13:202:14337:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:living over their lives. This will improve the wellbeing of these individuals and, as
13:203:14422:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:social welfare is the total of the wellbeing of individuals, it will increase welfare
13:204:14507:15:25:90:162:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:across society.
13:205:14522:25:15:90:504:400:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This paper uses innovative economic analysis to examine the scale of this increase in
13:206:14607:15:15:90:504:385:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people’s  wellbeing.  It  finds  that  if  people  save  for  retirement  through  personal
13:207:14698:15:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts, then generally their wellbeing will be enhanced. As more people delay
13:208:14777:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:spending their income from when they are in work to when they are in retirement,
13:209:14857:15:0:90:496:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:we will feel better off as a society because of the increase in individual wellbeing.
14:210:14962:0:52:90:299:560:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:1   Introduction
14:211:14978:52:26:90:214:508:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.1Background
14:212:14991:26:15:90:504:482:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f9:The  Government  White  Paper  Security  in  retirement:  towards  a  new  pensions
14:213:15074:15:15:90:504:467:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:system1,  published  in  May  2006,  contained  a  pension  reform  package  that  is
14:214:15159:15:15:90:504:452:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:designed to provide a long-lasting framework. It also announced the intention to
14:215:15239:15:15:90:504:437:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:produce  this  technical  paper,  to  assess  in  more  detail  the  economic  and  social
14:216:15329:15:15:90:504:422:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare  impacts  of  two  particular  aspects  of  the  reforms,  the  introduction  of
14:217:15417:15:15:90:504:407:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts and measures to extend working life. This paper explores possible
14:218:15500:15:15:90:504:392:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:methodological approaches to how the economic and social welfare effects could
14:219:15578:15:15:90:504:377:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:be measured and using these methodologies provides quantitative estimates. This
14:220:15657:15:15:90:504:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:paper is not a definitive statement on the magnitude of outcomes from pension
14:221:15734:15:15:90:504:347:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reform, about which there is substantial uncertainty, but suggests the direction and
14:222:15818:15:25:90:231:332:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:possible scale of the effects.
14:223:15848:25:15:90:504:307:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:A number of challenges to the current pension system were identified in the White
14:224:15929:15:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Paper. It concluded that pension reform is needed to address demographic and
14:225:16005:15:15:90:504:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:social change, the large number of people who are undersaving for retirement and
14:226:16085:15:15:90:504:262:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the complexity of and the inequalities inherent in the State Pension system. To cope
14:227:16169:15:15:90:504:247:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with these challenges, as well as improve outcomes for individuals and society as a
14:228:16252:15:22:90:425:232:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:whole, the White Paper announced the following policy measures:
14:229:16315:22:15:90:504:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The uprating of the basic State Pension with earnings rather than prices and the
14:230:16398:15:22:102:406:195:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reform of the State Second Pension into a flat rate pension;
14:231:16458:22:15:90:504:173:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The improvement of coverage by the basic State Pension by reducing the number
14:232:16538:15:15:102:505:158:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of years of contributions necessary to qualify and the introduction of new credits
14:233:16620:15:23:102:153:143:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:for carers;
14:234:16631:23:15:90:504:120:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The gradual increase in the State Pension age and the consideration of other
14:235:16710:15:15:102:505:105:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:measures to extend working life, such as greater flexibility around State Pension
14:236:16791:15:39:102:145:90:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:deferral;
14:237:16800:39:18:90:505:51:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:1Department for Work and Pensions (DWP), 2006. Hereafter referred to as the
14:238:16875:18:0:102:168:33:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:White Paper.
15:239:16887:0:106:19:26:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:6
15:240:16900:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The introduction of personal accounts to enable and encourage individuals who
15:241:16980:15:22:102:333:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:are not currently saving to start to do so; and
15:242:17027:22:15:90:504:678:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The  streamlining  of  the  regulatory  environment,  including  the  abolition  of
15:243:17113:15:26:102:400:663:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contracting out for defined contribution pension schemes.
15:244:17170:26:15:90:504:637:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The impacts of the increase in the State Pension age and the introduction of personal
15:245:17255:15:37:90:416:622:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts will be analysed in detail in the remainder of this paper.
15:246:17322:37:21:90:483:585:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.2Increasing State Pension age and extending working
15:247:17375:21:25:133:153:564:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:life
15:248:17379:25:15:90:504:539:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Life expectancy has improved considerably since State retirement pensions were first
15:249:17463:15:15:90:504:524:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:introduced, and is projected to continue to do so into the future. Despite this trend,
15:250:17549:15:15:90:504:509:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the average age of exit from the labour market fell from the 1950s to the mid-1990s.
15:251:17633:15:15:90:504:494:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Although this trend has shown signs of reversal in recent years, the average age of
15:252:17716:15:15:90:504:479:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:retirement remains below historical levels. For example, in 1950 men retired at 67 on
15:253:17801:15:15:90:504:464:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:average and women at 64. By contrast, comparable figures for the present day show
15:254:17882:15:15:90:504:449:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:an  average  retirement  age  of  64  and  62  respectively  (see  Figure  1.1),  while  life
15:255:17975:15:33:90:436:434:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expectancy at 65 in 2006 was almost nine years longer than in 1950.
15:256:18042:33:0:90:432:401:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 1.1Trends in mean age of retirement in the UK
16:257:18095:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Continuing increases in life expectancy mean that were State Pension age to remain
16:258:18177:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:fixed  at  its  present  level,  the  current  State  Pension  system  would  be  paying  for
16:259:18270:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:progressively  longer  retirements.  Increasing  State  Pension  age  in  response  to
16:260:18356:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increasing longevity, as announced in the White Paper, is intended to ensure that
16:261:18437:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the state retirement pension system can provide a sound foundation for working
16:262:18515:15:25:90:308:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and saving decisions on a sustainable basis.
16:263:18559:25:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The increase in State Pension age will, however, need to be accompanied by cultural
16:264:18642:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and behavioural changes around retirement to produce an increase in the average
16:265:18721:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:retirement age. Working longer is the logical response to an ageing population. On
16:266:18803:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:an individual basis working longer enables individuals to build up greater savings for
16:267:18889:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:retirement and can stabilise the length of time spent in retirement. Additionally, the
16:268:18975:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:more people who are in work and contributing to the growth of the economy, the
16:269:19053:15:25:90:498:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:more funds there will be available to support those people who are in retirement.
16:270:19134:25:15:90:504:500:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State Pension age may influence the retirement decision through two channels. The
16:271:19215:15:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:first is that the State Pension age is set at a specific age defined by the Government
16:272:19301:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and, therefore, creates a culture of expectation of retiring at that age. The second is
16:273:19388:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that  upon  reaching  State  Pension  age,  individuals  have  access  to  an  additional
16:274:19477:15:25:90:467:440:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:source of income, thus giving people the financial means to stop working.2
16:275:19551:25:15:90:504:415:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:While State Pension age is important in influencing people’s retirement decision it is
16:276:19637:15:15:90:504:400:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:only one factor determining the timing of retirement. The most common retirement
16:277:19717:15:15:90:504:385:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:ages are 60 for women and 65 for men – the current State Pension ages – (see Figure
16:278:19800:15:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:1.2) suggesting the importance of State Pension age in signalling or as a cultural
16:279:19882:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reference  point  in  determining  retirement  behaviour.  But  labour  market  activity
16:280:19970:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rates show a decline from age 55 onwards demonstrating that other factors are also
16:281:20052:15:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:important.  Almost  half  of  all  men  exit  the  labour  market  before  reaching  State
16:282:20142:15:25:90:234:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Pension age (see Figure 1.3).
16:283:20171:25:15:90:504:285:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  Government  has  already  put  in  place  or  planned  a  number  of  measures
16:284:20254:15:15:90:504:270:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:intended  to  change  the  culture  and  behaviour  surrounding  retirement.  These
16:285:20337:15:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:include the New Deal 50 plus employment programme to help older workers, the
16:286:20413:15:15:90:504:240:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:Age Positive campaign, the Be Ready promotional campaign to raise awareness
16:287:20488:15:15:90:504:225:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:ahead of the introduction of age discrimination legislation in October 2006, more
16:288:20569:15:15:90:504:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:generous increments in the State Pension when deferring it and equalisation of
16:289:20647:15:139:90:417:195:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State Pension age for men and women between 2010 and 2020.
16:290:20717:139:0:90:221:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2Humphrey et al., 2003.
17:291:20740:0:105:19:26:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:8
17:292:20741:105:14:90:497:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 1.2Average annual decline in activity rates of single-year
17:293:20806:14:328:175:220:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:cohorts

18:295:20879:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  White  Paper also  proposes  a  number  of  measures  to  extend  working  life
18:296:20962:15:22:90:140:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:including:
18:297:20972:22:15:90:504:678:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Consideration of how State Pension deferral might in the future offer greater
18:298:21052:15:15:102:505:663:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:flexibility, both in terms of the amount drawn and deferred, and allowing people
18:299:21132:15:22:102:446:648:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:more flexibility to move in and out of work after State Pension age;
18:300:21200:22:15:90:504:626:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Providing  improved  communications  and  information  in  support  of  longer
18:301:21281:15:23:102:170:611:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working; and
18:302:21293:23:15:90:504:588:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Working in partnership with employers to encourage them to retain older workers,
18:303:21376:15:25:102:381:573:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and to offer them greater flexibility around retirement.
18:304:21432:25:15:90:504:548:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f9:The recent Government publication, A new deal for welfare: Empowering people to
18:305:21511:15:15:90:504:533:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:work3,  also  proposes  a  series  of  measures  to  boost  support  for  older  people
18:306:21598:15:15:90:504:518:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:returning to work and to improve the information available about options for work
18:307:21678:15:15:90:504:503:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and retirement. These include aligning employment support for older long-term
18:308:21755:15:15:90:504:488:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:unemployed people with that for younger age groups, improving back-to-work
18:309:21829:15:15:90:504:473:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:support for Jobseeker’s Allowance claimants and their dependent partners who are
18:310:21909:15:15:90:504:458:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:over 50 and piloting of face-to-face guidance sessions with people approaching 50
18:311:21990:15:25:90:129:443:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:or over.
18:312:21998:25:15:90:504:418:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The measures outlined above should provide greater support for those wishing to
18:313:22077:15:38:90:487:403:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:continue in work for longer and those older workers seeking to return to work.
18:314:22155:38:25:90:254:365:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.3Personal accounts
18:315:22175:25:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In  the  White  Paper,  the  Government  proposed  the  introduction  of  a  system  of
18:316:22262:15:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts in 2012. This policy aims to enable individuals not already in a
18:317:22344:15:15:90:504:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pension scheme to make their own low cost retirement provision. Eligible employees
18:318:22426:15:15:90:504:295:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:will be automatically enrolled into the new scheme or an existing employer scheme,
18:319:22508:15:15:90:504:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:but have the right to opt out if they wish to. Participants will make contributions
18:320:22591:15:15:90:504:265:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:along with their employers and the State4. These contributions will be on a defined
18:321:22674:15:15:90:504:250:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contribution  basis,  in  which  the  fund  at  retirement  will  depend  on  the  level  of
18:322:22766:15:15:90:504:235:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contributions and fund growth during the accumulation phase. Individuals will have
18:323:22848:15:15:90:504:220:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:appropriate levels of choice over how to invest their funds. The accounts will be
18:324:22929:15:15:90:504:205:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:portable  between  employers  and  between  periods  of  employment  and  self-
18:325:23008:15:85:90:157:190:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment.
18:326:23019:85:20:90:164:105:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:3DWP, 2005.
18:327:23030:20:18:90:505:85:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:4Employers will have the choice whether to automatically enrol employees into
18:328:23107:18:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts or into a different employer-sponsored scheme that qualifies
18:329:23185:14:0:102:177:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:for exemption.
19:330:23199:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:10
19:331:23213:106:22:90:198:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The new scheme will:
19:332:23233:22:15:90:504:693:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Significantly  increase  the  number  of  people  currently  saving  for  retirement.
19:333:23321:15:15:102:505:678:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Modelling  suggests  that  around  ten  million  employees  could  be  newly
19:334:23397:15:15:102:505:663:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:automatically enrolled into a personal account. In addition to this, it is estimated
19:335:23481:15:15:102:505:648:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that a further 0.7 million employees who work for an employer who currently
19:336:23556:15:15:102:505:633:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:offers an adequate employer pension scheme, but are not members, could be
19:337:23629:15:15:102:505:618:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:automatically enrolled into their employer scheme. In total, it is estimated that
19:338:23710:15:15:102:505:603:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:10.8 million employees could be automatically enrolled into a pension following
19:339:23789:15:15:102:505:588:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the reform. Once assumptions are made about the number of employees who
19:340:23860:15:15:102:505:573:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:are likely to opt out of personal accounts and allowed for opt in membership by
19:341:23939:15:15:102:505:558:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  self  employed,  the  central  estimate  of  the  number  of  people  in  personal
19:342:24026:15:15:102:505:543:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts  is  around  eight  million.  In  addition  around  an  additional  0.3  million
19:343:24115:15:15:102:505:528:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employees  would  be  automatically  enrolled  and  would  not  opt  out  of  their
19:344:24198:15:22:102:403:513:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employer scheme once automatic enrolment is introduced.
19:345:24253:22:15:90:504:491:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Have low charges so that individuals keep more of their savings. The management
19:346:24335:15:15:102:505:476:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:charges on personal accounts would be lower than on most currently available
19:347:24411:15:15:102:505:461:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal pensions: the current charge cap for annual management charges for
19:348:24486:15:15:102:505:446:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:stakeholder pensions is 1.5 per cent in the first ten years falling to one per cent
19:349:24569:15:15:102:505:431:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:per  year  after  that.  Occupational  pension  schemes  and  some  group  personal
19:350:24652:15:15:102:505:416:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pension schemes are able to achieve administrative charges equivalent to around
19:351:24731:15:15:102:505:401:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:0.3 to 0.5 per cent or less. Therefore, people automatically enrolled into these
19:352:24811:15:26:102:325:386:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:schemes will also benefit from low charges.
19:353:24854:26:22:90:285:360:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The key features of the scheme will be:
19:354:24893:22:15:90:504:338:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  An organisational structure that ensures low charges and good-quality service
19:355:24973:15:22:102:177:323:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:for individuals;
19:356:24989:22:15:90:504:301:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Automatic  enrolment  for  all  eligible  employees,  but  with  the  freedom  to  opt
19:357:25078:15:23:102:123:286:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:out;
19:358:25082:23:15:90:504:263:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  A  minimum  overall  level  of  contribution  from  employers,  employees  and  the
19:359:25168:15:15:102:505:248:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Government,  to  promote  a  minimum  level  of  pension  saving,  with  people
19:360:25247:15:15:102:505:233:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:encouraged to contribute more. The minimum overall contribution is eight per
19:361:25323:15:15:102:505:218:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:cent of earnings between around £5,000 and £33,000, the split of contributions
19:362:25401:15:21:102:167:203:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is as follows:
19:363:25415:21:22:102:310:182:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:–  employers contributing three per cent;
19:364:25456:22:21:102:329:160:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:–  employees contributing four per cent; and
19:365:25500:21:14:102:505:139:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:–  the State contributing one per cent as normal tax relief, as under the current
19:366:25581:14:40:113:144:125:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:rules;5
19:367:25588:40:18:90:505:85:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:5One per cent represents basic rate tax relief on individuals’ contributions – in
19:368:25669:18:14:102:504:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:addition, individuals may be entitled to higher-rate tax relief and neither employers
19:369:25754:14:15:102:505:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:nor  employees  pay  tax  or  National  Insurance  contributions  on  employer
19:370:25832:15:0:102:173:38:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contributions.
20:371:25860:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  A national minimum employer contribution, increasing incentives to save. For all
20:372:25943:15:15:102:505:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employees, whether they access pension saving through personal accounts or
20:373:26017:15:15:102:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:existing  pension  provision,  if  they  remain  in  the  scheme  they  will  receive  a
20:374:26105:15:15:102:505:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:minimum employer contribution of three per cent of earnings between around
20:375:26179:15:22:102:212:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:£5,000 and £33,000;
20:376:26198:22:15:90:504:633:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Opt-in access available to those not automatically enrolled, including the self-
20:377:26281:15:23:102:178:618:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employed; and
20:378:26294:23:15:90:504:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Portable and flexible accounts, to fit in with modern life and the greater likelihood
20:379:26382:15:38:102:268:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of people moving between jobs.
20:380:26412:38:25:90:332:542:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.4Measuring impacts of policies
20:381:26444:25:15:90:504:517:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This report will look at two different ways of measuring the impact of the increase in
20:382:26530:15:15:90:504:502:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State  Pension  age  and  the  introduction  of  personal  accounts.  We  first  consider
20:383:26619:15:15:90:504:487:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic effects, in the context of which two complementary approaches are used.
20:384:26699:15:15:90:504:472:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The first is a partial approach that can quickly provide estimates of the economic
20:385:26781:15:15:90:504:457:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects based on assumptions around changes in employment rates. The second
20:386:26856:15:15:90:504:442:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:method is more comprehensive and uses NiGEM, a macroeconomic model of the UK
20:387:26932:15:15:90:504:427:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economy  developed  by  the  National  Institute  of  Economic  and  Social  Research
20:388:27017:15:15:90:504:412:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:(NIESR),  to  analyse  these  effects.  Finally  we  develop  an  innovative  method  to
20:389:27105:15:37:90:470:397:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimate the social welfare impact of the introduction of personal accounts.
20:390:27181:37:26:90:255:360:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.5Economic impacts
20:391:27200:26:15:90:504:334:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In measuring the economic impacts we are looking at how the reform impacts on
20:392:27277:15:15:90:504:319:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  size  of  the  economy  or  national  income,  as  either  measured  by  the  gross
20:393:27365:15:15:90:504:304:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:domestic product (GDP), which is a measure of the total value of final goods and
20:394:27445:15:15:90:504:289:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:services produced within a country’s borders in a year, or gross national product
20:395:27526:15:15:90:504:274:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:(GNP) which is the value of all goods and services produced in a country in one year,
20:396:27611:15:25:90:504:259:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:plus income earned by its residents abroad, minus income payable to non-residents.
20:397:27693:25:15:90:504:234:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:If total economic resources are increased, this means that more income is potentially
20:398:27778:15:15:90:504:219:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:available  to  individuals  for  consumption.  Chapter  2  looks  at  a  simple  partial
20:399:27866:15:15:90:504:204:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:equilibrium model to estimate the impact of increasing State Pension age, while
20:400:27945:15:15:90:504:189:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Chapter 3 uses a dynamic general equilibrium model of the economy to measure the
20:401:28025:15:15:90:504:174:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impacts of both State Pension age changes and increases in saving on the size of the
20:402:28109:15:37:90:140:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economy.
20:403:28117:37:26:90:241:122:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.6Welfare impacts
20:404:28135:26:15:90:504:96:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The aim of many reforms of public policy is to make society as a whole feel better off
20:405:28221:15:15:90:504:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:or, in other words, to increase social welfare. To gain insight into the aggregate
20:406:28303:15:15:90:504:66:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:concept of social welfare, analysing individual welfare, or utility (an economists’
20:407:28386:15:0:90:493:51:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:term for describing an individual’s or a society’s wellbeing), is a useful approach.
21:408:28470:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:12
21:409:28484:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Research6 suggests that, while utility is not identical to the more comprehensible
21:410:28566:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:term  happiness,  the  two  concepts  are  closely  related.  Utility  is  by  no  means
21:411:28654:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:straightforward to measure. It is influenced by a vast number of factors, some of
21:412:28735:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:them intangible. Furthermore, each individual attaches different values to certain
21:413:28817:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:things. For example, one person may accumulate as many goods as possible to
21:414:28892:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:maximise their wellbeing, while another’s happiness may derive from the knowledge
21:415:28973:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that she lives in an environment where her rights are protected by sound institutions
21:416:29058:15:25:90:344:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and she receives good healthcare when necessary.
21:417:29106:25:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:For  analytical  purposes,  consumption  of  goods  and  services  including  leisure  is
21:418:29195:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:usually the main component of utility. This is an abstraction from reality but it is
21:419:29279:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:useful  in  a  model  context.  Furthermore,  research  has  found  that  income  and
21:420:29364:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:happiness  are  correlated,  making  income  an  imperfect  yet  useful  indicator  for
21:421:29451:15:25:90:286:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:happiness and overall levels of welfare.
21:422:29491:25:15:90:504:500:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Our model estimates social welfare by aggregating the welfare of all individuals in
21:423:29574:15:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:society. In doing so, we assume a utilitarian point of view, that is, we do not attach
21:424:29660:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different weights to different individuals, for example, according to their income
21:425:29742:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:before  reforms.  Instead  we  simply  add  all  changes  in  wellbeing  to  arrive  at  our
21:426:29834:15:25:90:196:440:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:aggregate measure.7
21:427:29853:25:15:90:504:415:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:According to standard economic theory individuals are best off making independent
21:428:29934:15:15:90:504:400:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption choices. In other words, individuals, in theory, buy the goods and
21:429:30012:15:15:90:504:385:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:services that for them have the biggest impact on wellbeing, as well as accurately
21:430:30094:15:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:forecasting how much income they will earn, how much they will want to consume
21:431:30172:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in  the  future  and  save  accordingly.  They  would  thereby  maximise  individual
21:432:30256:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:wellbeing,  and  with  it  social  welfare,  leaving  no  reason  for  the  government  to
21:433:30346:15:25:90:141:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:intervene.
21:434:30356:25:15:90:504:300:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In  practice,  however,  the  government  will,  at  a  minimum,  find  justification  for
21:435:30446:15:15:90:504:285:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:intervening in the market due to the existence of public goods, for which there is a
21:436:30530:15:15:90:504:270:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:demand but which cannot be efficiently supplied by the private sector, for example
21:437:30612:15:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:national defence. Even beyond the provision of public goods, however, it takes a
21:438:30692:15:15:90:504:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:very specific set of circumstances in which the market and hence the individuals in it
21:439:30778:15:15:90:504:225:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:will  produce  welfare  maximising  results.  In  reality,  welfare  will  not  always  be
21:440:30868:15:22:90:422:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:maximised in a general sense due to one of the following reasons:
21:441:30933:22:15:90:504:188:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Imperfect information: consumers are unable to fully compare all available goods
21:442:31016:15:15:102:505:173:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in terms of their prices and quality, which may prevent them from making the
21:443:31092:15:15:102:505:158:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:most efficient consumption decisions. They also cannot fully predict their income
21:444:31173:15:15:102:505:143:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and  prices  of  goods  in  the  future,  which  is  especially  relevant  for  retirement
21:445:31263:15:37:102:150:128:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pensions.
21:446:31272:37:20:90:221:91:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:6Frey and Stutzer, 2002.
21:447:31296:20:18:90:505:71:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:7As opposed to, e.g. the Rawlsian view which regards an increase in income of
21:448:31373:18:15:102:505:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:one  individual  as  insignificant  for  social  welfare  if  the  worst  off  individual  of
21:449:31466:15:0:102:384:38:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:society does not also experience an increase in income.
22:450:31535:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The development of behavioural economics is extending our understanding of
22:451:31612:15:15:102:505:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the cause of imperfect outcomes. For example, it suggests that even if perfect
22:452:31690:15:15:102:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:information exists many people do not make the right decisions due to complexity
22:453:31770:15:22:102:267:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:or short-sightedness and inertia.
22:454:31803:22:15:90:504:648:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Imperfect competition: for example monopoly or collusion that lead to inefficiently
22:455:31889:15:23:102:161:633:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:high prices.
22:456:31901:23:15:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Externalities: where an activity by one person produces an unwanted side effect
22:457:31983:15:15:102:505:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:for another person, such as pollution, in which case the Government may decide
22:458:32061:15:22:102:211:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to impose regulation.
22:459:32082:22:15:90:504:558:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Increasing returns to scale: this means that it will be most efficient to let a single
22:460:32171:15:23:102:505:543:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:producer provide a good or service, due to substantial set-up cost or a network.
22:461:32251:23:15:90:504:520:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The  government  may  also  decide  to  intervene  to  increase  social  justice  and
22:462:32339:15:25:102:318:505:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:redistribute income via the benefit system.
22:463:32382:25:15:90:504:480:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Due to one or more of these issues the government may choose to intervene so as to
22:464:32464:15:15:90:504:465:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:create an environment within which society as a whole can achieve a higher level of
22:465:32547:15:15:90:504:450:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare. In the final chapter of this paper on social welfare estimates of personal
22:466:32630:15:15:90:504:435:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts  we  show  how  these  issues  apply  in  the  case  of  pension  saving  and,
22:467:32717:15:37:90:366:420:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:therefore, estimate the welfare gain from intervention.
22:468:32772:37:26:90:294:383:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.7What is not in the paper
22:469:32799:26:15:90:504:357:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As we will discuss in Chapter 4, accurately estimating the welfare impacts of longer
22:470:32883:15:15:90:504:342:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working  lives  would  require  developing  a  model  to  take  account  of  individual
22:471:32970:15:15:90:504:327:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:preferences amongst those affected by the change, something which would be an
22:472:33047:15:15:90:504:312:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:extremely challenging project and beyond the scope of this paper. Neither do we
22:473:33126:15:15:90:504:297:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimate the welfare impacts of the overall increases in the size of the economy as a
22:474:33211:15:25:90:463:282:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:result of the changes in State Pension age and increases in pension saving.
22:475:33286:25:15:90:504:257:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This paper does not look at the impact of the reforms to State Pensions. The White
22:476:33368:15:15:90:504:242:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Paper contained significant analysis of the impact on individuals and distributional
22:477:33452:15:15:90:504:227:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects. It is outside of the scope of this paper to attempt to analyse the state reform
22:478:33540:15:15:90:504:212:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes using the methods applied here. To measure the impact of changes in the
22:479:33619:15:15:90:504:197:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State Pension a model would have to estimate the welfare effects of receiving a
22:480:33698:15:15:90:504:182:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:higher income, which is less means-tested, for a slightly shorter period, instead of
22:481:33782:15:15:90:504:167:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the current state system. This would require a different model and the evaluation of
22:482:33866:15:0:90:314:152:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different factors affecting individual welfare.
23:483:33913:0:110:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:14
23:484:33927:110:25:90:340:711:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:1.8Outline of the rest of the paper
23:485:33962:25:15:90:504:686:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This paper is divided into three further chapters which explore a methodological
23:486:34042:15:15:90:504:671:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:approach to estimating the impact of pension reform. Each chapter takes a different
23:487:34125:15:15:90:504:656:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:approach  to  look  at  the  impact  of  the  increase  in  State  Pension  age  and  the
23:488:34214:15:15:90:504:641:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:introduction of personal accounts and then quantifies the size of the impact using
23:489:34296:15:25:90:357:626:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:this methodology and a plausible set of assumptions.
23:490:34348:25:15:90:504:601:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Our estimates of the impact should not be taken as definitive: If different methods
23:491:34431:15:15:90:504:586:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:were adopted it would be possible for a different range of results to be produced.
23:492:34513:15:15:90:504:571:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The methodological approaches taken in this paper are innovative and, as the nature
23:493:34596:15:15:90:504:556:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of this paper should be seen as consultative, we welcome other views on the issues
23:494:34678:15:0:90:144:541:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:presented.
24:495:34750:0:39:90:400:562:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:2   Economic impact of
24:496:34772:39:38:133:386:523:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:working longer – a
24:497:34790:38:53:133:475:485:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:microeconomic approach
24:498:34812:53:25:90:216:432:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:2.1Introduction
24:499:34827:25:15:90:504:407:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f9:The  Government’s  White  Paper  Security  in  retirement:  towards  a  new  pensions
24:500:34912:15:15:90:504:392:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:system includes proposals to raise State Pension age from 65 to 68 between 2024
24:501:34991:15:15:90:504:377:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and 2046. This chapter looks at how this policy change, combined with measures to
24:502:35072:15:25:90:376:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:extend working life, may contribute to economic output.
24:503:35127:25:15:90:504:337:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The general introduction provided some background to the proposed changes in
24:504:35203:15:15:90:504:322:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State  Pension  age  and  on  the  broader  Extending  Working  Life  agenda.  In  this
24:505:35290:15:15:90:504:307:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:chapter, the impact on GDP of the changes to State Pension age combined with
24:506:35366:15:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:measures  to  extend  working  life  are  estimated  from  the  possible  employment
24:507:35450:15:37:90:210:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impacts of the changes.
24:508:35473:37:26:90:276:240:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:2.2Analytical framework
24:509:35496:26:15:90:504:214:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The general introduction set out the role working longer has in society’s response to
24:510:35581:15:15:90:504:199:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  challenge  of  an  ageing  population.  There  are  also  likely  to  be  benefits  to
24:511:35672:15:25:90:331:184:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals and employers from working longer.
24:512:35718:25:15:90:504:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:For employers, with 40 per cent of the workforce expected to be age 45 and over by
24:513:35800:15:15:90:504:144:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2010,  business  productivity  and  competitiveness  is  increasingly  dependent  on
24:514:35884:15:15:90:504:129:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:maximising  the  contribution  of  older  people.  However,  many  employers  hold
24:515:35966:15:15:90:504:114:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:outdated beliefs that younger workers are more productive than older ones, and
24:516:36044:15:15:90:504:99:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:discriminate  against  older  people  in  recruitment  and  training.  This  means  that
24:517:36132:15:15:90:504:84:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:current  retirement  patterns  can  prematurely  disenfranchise  healthy  and  able
24:518:36215:15:15:90:504:69:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people,  who  want  to  continue  working,  from  the  active  labour  market.  These
24:519:36300:15:15:90:504:54:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people’s productive value to the economy is lost, and their skills and knowledge are
24:520:36384:15:0:90:179:39:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:lost to employers.
25:521:36402:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:16
25:522:36464:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Evidence on the productivity of older workers (based on those aged 50–69) suggests
25:523:36546:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that they are no less productive than younger workers, except in a limited range of
25:524:36629:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:jobs requiring rapid reaction or physical strength that people tend to move out of as
25:525:36714:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:they become older. Reduction in physical capability and work ability is probably
25:526:36794:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:inevitable  with  age,  but  chronological  age  is  not  a  reliable  marker.  Many  older
25:527:36885:15:25:90:406:640:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:workers are capable of continuing to work and want to do so.8
25:528:36946:25:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Only  where  older  workers  do  not  receive  the  same  level  of  training  as  younger
25:529:37036:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:workers doing the same kind of work does their performance show differences.
25:530:37112:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Older  workers  receiving  appropriate  job-related  training  reach  the  same  skill
25:531:37198:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:standards  as  younger  workers.  Evidence  suggests  that  a  reduction  in  speed  or
25:532:37285:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:strength is offset by aspects of working that improve with experience, for instance,
25:533:37369:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:prioritisation, planning, troubleshooting and motivation. And, technological change
25:534:37452:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is reducing the proportion of jobs involving heavy manual work, for example, in the
25:535:37535:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:distribution  sector  where  technology  and  automation  has  greatly  reduced  the
25:536:37619:15:25:90:283:495:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:amount of physical exertion required.9
25:537:37657:25:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:However, barriers still exist in terms of access to training for older workers. Evidence
25:538:37745:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:suggests that training is less likely to be offered to older individuals. The likelihood of
25:539:37836:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:someone aged over 55 participating in training is 50 per cent less than that for an
25:540:37919:15:15:90:504:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:adult aged 35-44 and for employed adults training decreases markedly beyond the
25:541:37998:15:15:90:504:410:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:age of 60.10 Other evidence shows that encouragement from employers to train
25:542:38074:15:25:90:246:395:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:tended to tail off after 50-54.11
25:543:38107:25:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:From the point of view of the individual, delaying their retirement affords them the
25:544:38191:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:opportunity to benefit from more earnings and from the opportunity to save more
25:545:38270:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:for when they do decide to retire. Increasing State Pension age may have a role to
25:546:38352:15:25:90:372:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:play in assisting the individual in realising these benefits.
25:547:38413:25:15:90:504:300:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:A relatively high number of individuals retire early with little consideration of the
25:548:38498:15:15:90:504:285:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:financial implications of their decision. For example, when asked about the factors
25:549:38581:15:15:90:504:270:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:they consider when retiring, just under a third (31 per cent) of those not forced into
25:550:38667:15:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:early retirement considered the immediate financial implications. A similarly low
25:551:38748:15:15:90:504:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:proportion considered the longer-term financial implications.12 This finding, combined
25:552:38834:15:15:90:504:225:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with the extent of under-saving for retirement as discussed in Chapter 4 on personal
25:553:38918:15:30:90:504:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts, suggests that, at present, some individuals may be making sub-optimal
25:554:38997:30:18:90:505:180:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:8Smeaton  and  McKay,  2003,  for  instance,  find  that  men  working  post-State
25:555:39079:18:15:102:505:162:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Pension age are under represented in the construction and manufacturing sectors.
25:556:39159:15:14:102:505:147:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:They  conclude  that,  as  many  of  the  jobs  in  these  sectors  require  a  degree  of
25:557:39249:14:16:102:503:133:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:physical strength, employers may regard them as unsuitable for older workers.
25:558:39326:16:20:90:210:117:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:9See Meadows, 2004.
25:559:39345:20:20:90:208:97:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:10Newton et al., 2005.
25:560:39367:20:21:90:221:77:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:11Humphrey et al., 2003.
25:561:39391:21:0:90:221:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:12Humphrey et al., 2003.
26:562:39477:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:decisions regarding their retirement. These individuals are leaving the labour market
26:563:39562:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earlier than they would if they had more information on the financial implications
26:564:39644:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and their life expectancy than they have at present. In fact, evidence suggests that
26:565:39728:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals tend to underestimate their life expectancy significantly. This point will
26:566:39814:15:25:90:457:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:be addressed explicitly in the next chapter on macroeconomic modelling.
26:567:39885:25:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Raising State Pension age might increase employment in a number of ways. If some
26:568:39965:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people retire too early due to information failures then increasing State Pension age
26:569:40050:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:may help to overcome this by signalling to them that they need to work longer than
26:570:40132:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:they otherwise thought. The reduction in income from later access to a State Pension
26:571:40216:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:may also result in individuals working for longer. Table 2.1 provides some indication
26:572:40301:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of the extent to which retirement decisions are driven by expectations and financial
26:573:40385:15:33:90:167:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:considerations.
26:574:40400:33:29:90:471:507:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Table 2.1Reasons for expecting to retire at State Pension age
26:575:40461:29:20:90:472:478:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:ReasonTotal (percentage)
26:576:40485:20:15:90:436:458:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:It is the first opportunity to draw a state retirement pension39
26:577:40549:15:14:90:436:443:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:I always expected to57
26:578:40571:14:15:90:434:429:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:I couldn’t get another job after that age6
26:579:40613:15:15:90:436:414:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:I could afford to retire then28
26:580:40644:15:19:90:434:399:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Other9
26:581:40650:19:18:90:337:380:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Note: Multiple responses; percentages do not sum to 100.
26:582:40706:18:28:90:430:362:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Source: Factors affecting the labour market participation of older workers, DWP.
26:583:40786:28:15:90:504:334:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:However,  estimating  the  social  welfare  effect  of  working  longer  would  require
26:584:40873:15:15:90:504:319:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounting for the cost of reduced leisure both for those making optimal and those
26:585:40955:15:15:90:504:304:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:making  sub-optimal  retirement  decisions.  Measuring  the  welfare  impact  of  the
26:586:41040:15:15:90:504:289:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reform  would,  therefore,  require  some  estimation  of  the  utility/disutility  of
26:587:41126:15:15:90:504:274:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment  for  the  different  individuals  affected.  However,  no  estimates  are
26:588:41211:15:15:90:504:259:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:available, however, for the extent of the work/leisure trade-off or how to account for
26:589:41297:15:15:90:504:244:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:differing  preferences  across  the  affected  population.  Estimation  of  the  welfare
26:590:41385:15:15:90:504:229:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impact  would  entail  developing  a  model  to  take  account  of  these  preferences,
26:591:41472:15:15:90:504:214:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:something that would be an extremely challenging project and beyond the scope of
26:592:41552:15:25:90:143:199:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:this paper.
26:593:41563:25:15:90:504:174:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:There may also be a number of non-financial benefits from working longer, which
26:594:41642:15:15:90:504:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:will generate welfare benefits that cannot be easily measured. Research suggests
26:595:41722:15:15:90:504:144:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that personal relationships and social networks may be important considerations in
26:596:41804:15:15:90:504:129:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:decisions about whether or when to retire. Irving et al. (2005) found that work
26:597:41883:15:15:90:504:114:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:provided a social life and social contact for many respondents, particularly those
26:598:41965:15:15:90:504:99:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:who were single, widowed or divorced. This was particularly true for people with
26:599:42045:15:15:90:504:84:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:health conditions. The researchers also found that a number of respondents cited
26:600:42125:15:15:90:504:69:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the physical and psychological benefits to the individual of remaining in work. They
26:601:42209:15:0:90:504:54:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:included self-esteem and pride, and mental and physical stimulation and activity,
27:602:42352:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which some respondents believed help them defer ageing.13 Studies also suggest
27:603:42430:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that re-employment for older workers can improve physical functioning and mental
27:604:42510:15:37:90:134:685:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:health.14
27:605:42519:37:26:90:224:648:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:2.3Methodology
27:606:42533:26:22:90:409:622:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is proposed that State Pension age will be increased in stages:
27:607:42599:22:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The first increase, from 65 to 66, to be phased in over two years, starting in April
27:608:42686:15:22:102:132:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2024;
27:609:42691:22:15:90:504:563:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The second increase, from 66 to 67, again phased in over two years, from April
27:610:42772:15:23:102:155:548:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2034; and
27:611:42781:23:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The third increase, from 67 to 68, also to be phased in over two years, from April
27:612:42866:15:25:102:132:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2044.
27:613:42871:25:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The starting point for estimating the GDP impact of these increases in State Pension
27:614:42955:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:age alongside measures to enable people to extend their working lives is to estimate
27:615:43039:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the likely employment increases resulting from the change. The estimates of the
27:616:43118:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increase in employment are then multiplied by assumptions about gross earnings to
27:617:43199:15:15:90:504:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimate the increase in labour income and a product market corrector is then used
27:618:43281:15:25:90:309:410:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:to scale this up to the full economic value.15
27:619:43327:25:15:90:504:385:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  approach  developed  to  estimate  the  employment  impacts  of  the  proposed
27:620:43410:15:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes was to consider possible upper and lower bound estimates of the likely
27:621:43488:15:25:90:128:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impact.
27:622:43495:25:15:90:504:330:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The lower bound estimate of the employment effect is based on the assumption that
27:623:43576:15:15:90:504:315:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:behaviour only changes at the ages affected by the State Pension age changes. That
27:624:43658:15:15:90:504:300:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is, when State Pension age rises from 65 to 66, only the behaviour of people aged 65
27:625:43742:15:15:90:504:285:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes in response. It is assumed that, as a result of the change, the change in the
27:626:43827:15:15:90:504:270:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment rate between 64 and 65 is kept the same as between 63 and 64. This
27:627:43904:15:25:90:398:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pattern is repeated for all age groups affected by the change.
27:628:43966:25:15:90:504:230:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The changes to State Pension age only impact on employment from 2024 when the
27:629:44043:15:15:90:504:215:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:first increase is introduced. Individuals do not alter their behaviour in anticipation of
27:630:44132:15:15:90:504:200:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the changes. When fully implemented (the State Pension age has increased to 68)
27:631:44211:15:15:90:504:185:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:only the behaviour of people aged 65, 66 and 67 is different to what it otherwise
27:632:44292:15:15:90:504:170:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:would have been. This is illustrated in Figures 2.1 and 2.2, where, under the lower
27:633:44375:15:23:90:380:155:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:bound estimate, employment only changes at these ages.
27:634:44429:23:20:90:221:132:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:13Humphrey et al., 2003.
27:635:44453:20:21:90:314:112:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:14Gallo et al., 2000, Frese and Mohr, 1987.
27:636:44496:21:18:90:505:91:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:15Note that this approach differs to that used to project long-term GDP levels in
27:637:44577:18:14:102:505:73:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:HM  Treasury’s  long-term  public  finance  report.  In  particular,  the  latter  uses
27:638:44664:14:15:102:505:59:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assumptions  concerning  aggregate  productivity  growth,  rather  than  gross
27:639:44742:15:14:102:505:44:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earnings,  to  derive  projected  GDP  levels  from  long-term  projections  of
27:640:44821:14:0:102:169:30:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment.
28:641:44894:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is possible, however, that this lower bound underestimates the impact of the
28:642:44973:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes. Behaviour may change at other ages as a result of the financial incentives
28:643:45056:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:created by the changes, as well as possible changes in retirement expectations as
28:644:45137:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:discussed  in  the  introduction. People  who  would  otherwise  retire  before  State
28:645:45222:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Pension age may now do so a little later as the period of retirement before access to
28:646:45307:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the State Pension becomes possible is now longer, similarly many who would retire
28:647:45388:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:after  State  Pension  age  may  now  work  even  later  in  life  to  increase  retirement
28:648:45479:15:23:90:131:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income.
28:649:45486:23:15:90:504:587:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  upper  estimate  of  the  effect  reflects  these  wider  impacts,  based  on  the
28:650:45573:15:15:90:504:572:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assumption that an individual’s exit from the labour market moves by the same
28:651:45650:15:15:90:504:557:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:amount as State Pension age. For estimation purposes, this assumption means that
28:652:45730:15:15:90:504:542:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the employment rates at a particular age are applied to the ages immediately above,
28:653:45813:15:15:90:504:527:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:as State Pension age increases. For example, in the case of the State Pension age
28:654:45894:15:15:90:504:512:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increase to 66, the employment rate for those aged 55 will be the same as for those
28:655:45977:15:15:90:504:497:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:aged 54. Between the ages of 56 and 65, employment rates are the same as they
28:656:46054:15:15:90:504:482:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:would have been a year previously had State Pension age not been increased (see
28:657:46133:15:15:90:504:467:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Figures 2.1 and 2.2). For example, for an individual aged 60, the employment rate
28:658:46214:15:15:90:504:452:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:will be the same as for an individual aged 59 before the increase in State Pension age
28:659:46300:15:24:90:196:437:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:has been factored in.
28:660:46321:24:15:90:504:413:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Under the upper bound estimates, it is assumed that the minimum age at which
28:661:46397:15:15:90:504:398:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:behaviour is affected is 55. This is the age at which, based on trends in age-specific
28:662:46483:15:15:90:504:383:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment  rates,  the  trend  towards  early  retirement  tends  to  become  clearly
28:663:46569:15:15:90:504:368:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:visible  (see  Figure  1.3).  Similarly,  it  is  assumed  that  there  is  no  impact  on  the
28:664:46664:15:15:90:504:353:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:participation and employment of those aged 70 and above. Given the low rates of
28:665:46743:15:15:90:504:338:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment among this group at present (see Table 2.2), any impact of the change
28:666:46823:15:31:90:205:323:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is likely to be marginal.
28:667:46848:31:14:90:503:292:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Table 2.2Current employment by five year age-bands; 55 and over
28:668:46911:14:30:161:223:278:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:age group

28:673:47065:18:28:90:286:177:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Source: Labour Force Survey, spring 2006, GB.
28:674:47110:28:15:90:504:149:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:One further aspect of this employment scenario is the timing of the behavioural
28:675:47189:15:15:90:504:134:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes.  While  the  first  change  to  State  Pension  age  is  not  proposed  to  be
28:676:47276:15:15:90:504:119:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:introduced until 2024, the estimates assume that people aged 55 and over will alter
28:677:47359:15:15:90:504:104:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their  behaviour  accordingly  so  someone  aged  55  in  2015,  who  would  have
28:678:47440:15:15:90:504:89:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:otherwise exited the labour market at 55, will alter their behaviour ahead of the
28:679:47521:15:24:90:190:74:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:anticipated change.
28:680:47540:24:15:90:504:50:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This might be an overestimation of the impact of the changes. It assumes no exit
28:681:47620:15:0:90:504:35:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:from the labour market over a three-year age range (ages 55, 56 and 57) once the
29:682:47762:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State Pension increase is fully implemented. A middle estimate based on an average
29:683:47844:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of the two estimates described above has been produced to arrive at a potentially
29:684:47925:15:23:90:304:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:more realistic estimate of the likely impact.
29:685:47970:23:15:90:504:662:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Figures 2.1 and 2.2 summarise the impact that raising State Pension age is estimated
29:686:48054:15:15:90:504:647:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to have on the employment rate of men and women aged 55-69 once increased to
29:687:48130:15:27:90:386:632:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:68 in 2046 under each of the three employment scenarios.
29:688:48186:27:293:90:415:605:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 2.1Projected employment rates 2050 – men
29:689:48233:293:0:90:435:312:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 2.2Projected employment rates 2050 – women
30:690:48344:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This  approach  gives  us  three  estimates  (upper,  middle  and  lower)  of  the  likely
30:691:48434:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment impact of the changes as shown in Figures 2.1 and 2.2. In estimating
30:692:48513:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  employment  impacts,  the  estimates  use  the  HM  Treasury  projections  of
30:693:48595:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment, developed for the 2005 pre-budget report, as their base.16 Equalisation
30:694:48678:15:25:90:466:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of State Pension age between 2010 and 2020 is factored into the baseline.
30:695:48751:25:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Under  each  of  the  three  scenarios  we  want  to  know  the  likely  contribution  to
30:696:48840:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic output that the estimated increases in employment will produce. To do
30:697:48918:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:so, we use the absolute increase in numbers employed combined with information
30:698:48996:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:on hours and earnings of the groups of workers affected by the change. Applying
30:699:49075:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimates of the annual gross earnings of workers affected under the estimates of
30:700:49156:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment change allows us to calculate an estimate of the annual aggregate
30:701:49232:15:25:90:393:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increase in labour income under each of the three scenarios.
30:702:49292:25:15:90:504:515:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Data on earnings and hours was sourced from the Labour Force Survey and based on
30:703:49372:15:15:90:504:500:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a four-quarter average (summer 2005 – spring 2006). Information on earnings and
30:704:49451:15:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:hours was obtained for the three age groups affected by the proposed changes;
30:705:49528:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:those aged 55-59, aged 60-64 and 65-69. To reflect the different earnings and
30:706:49605:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working patterns of men and women, this information was further broken down by
30:707:49683:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:gender for each of the three age groups. Changes in hours and earnings are more
30:708:49762:15:15:90:504:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:visible over five-year age bands than at individual ages while still allowing us to
30:709:49845:15:15:90:504:410:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reflect the changing earnings and working patterns of people as they approach
30:710:49922:15:25:90:496:395:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:State Pension age as well as those continuing to work beyond State Pension age.
30:711:50001:25:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The information on earnings and hours is, by its nature, retrospective. It is based on
30:712:50087:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the employment and working patterns of those aged 55-69 currently in the labour
30:713:50166:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:force. These may be subject to change in the future as working patterns change and
30:714:50248:15:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:older workers benefit from newly implemented extending working life measures
30:715:50324:15:15:90:504:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:such as age discrimination legislation. Therefore the estimates of hours and earnings
30:716:50409:15:15:90:504:295:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contained in this analysis have the potential to either under or overestimate future
30:717:50493:15:25:90:125:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:trends.
30:718:50500:25:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In  terms  of  underestimating  future  trends,  it  is  possible  that  the  older  workers
30:719:50592:15:15:90:504:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:affected by the changes to State Pension age may see an increase in gross earnings
30:720:50674:15:15:90:504:225:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and hours in the future. At present, a large portion of this group has the option of
30:721:50758:15:15:90:504:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:gradually moving into retirement by continuing to work beyond State Pension age at
30:722:50840:15:15:90:504:195:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reduced hours, but supplementing their income with State Pension income. After
30:723:50918:15:15:90:504:180:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the introduction of the proposed State Pension age increases the opportunity to
30:724:50997:15:15:90:504:165:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:supplement earnings with State Pension income will only be available to those aged
30:725:51079:15:15:90:504:150:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:68 and over. We may, therefore, see an increase in hours worked amongst the age
30:726:51158:15:78:90:298:135:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:group affected by the proposed changes.
30:727:51197:78:0:90:486:57:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:16See http://www.gad.gov.uk/ for the GAD 2004 based principal projections.
31:728:51271:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:22
31:729:51333:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:On the other hand, data on hours and earnings may be an overestimate of the future
31:730:51415:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:trends we are likely to see as a result of changes to State Pension age. The data on
31:731:51499:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:hours and earnings used in this analysis is based on those observed in the workplace
31:732:51583:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and might not fully be representative of all older people. Those who remain in work
31:733:51666:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:at present might be more productive than those whose work capacity is adversely
31:734:51745:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:affected by illness or disability. It may be that the employment of older workers in the
31:735:51833:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:future may feature less productive workers who may work for fewer hours or lower
31:736:51913:15:15:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earnings than those employed at present. It is also  conceivable that those who retire
31:737:51999:15:15:90:504:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:fully at present may not be able to do so in the future but may seek to retire gradually,
31:738:52088:15:25:90:371:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reducing their hours as they reach their retirement date.
31:739:52145:25:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Both of these are plausible scenarios, but are difficult to predict with any great
31:740:52227:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:certainty. In the absence of reliable evidence or information on how these trends
31:741:52308:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:might evolve in the future, past patterns of earnings and hours represent the best
31:742:52390:15:25:90:330:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimate of future earnings and hours available.
31:743:52438:25:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:To estimate the future gross earnings of those affected by the increase in State
31:744:52518:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Pension  age,  average  earnings  for  each  group  are  up-rated  by  estimated  real
31:745:52604:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earnings  growth  to  arrive  at  future  estimates  of  annual  gross  earnings.  For  the
31:746:52695:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:purpose  of  up-rating  earnings,  we  have  assumed  annual  real  wage  growth  of
31:747:52779:15:25:90:240:425:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:approximately two per cent.17
31:748:52808:25:15:90:504:400:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:To estimate the value of output produced by these additional workers, a product
31:749:52887:15:15:90:504:385:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:market corrector is used to scale up the increase in labour income resulting from the
31:750:52972:15:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reforms to the full economic value. This variable, used in economic effectiveness
31:751:53053:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:calculations, accounts for the value of workers output being divided between wages
31:752:53135:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and firms’ profits and is calculated as the inverse of the labour share of total factor
31:753:53222:15:25:90:480:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income. For the purpose of the analysis contained here it is estimated at 1.26.
31:754:53301:25:15:90:504:300:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Results of this analysis are presented in the results section below. The methodology
31:755:53385:15:15:90:504:285:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employed here is intended to estimate the impact on future GDP of increasing State
31:756:53467:15:15:90:504:270:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Pension age alongside measures to extend working life by estimating the employment
31:757:53549:15:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increases from these changes and reflecting the earnings and productivity profile of
31:758:53633:15:37:90:198:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the workers affected.
31:759:53654:37:26:90:429:203:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:2.4Limitations and weaknesses in methodology
31:760:53698:26:15:90:504:177:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:There is major uncertainty surrounding both future labour market projections and
31:761:53778:15:15:90:504:162:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the behavioural responses we expect in response to raising State Pension age and
31:762:53858:15:62:90:504:147:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accompanying measures to extend working life. In particular, forecasts of the likely
31:763:53942:62:18:90:505:85:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:17Given that baseline employment remains roughly constant between now and
31:764:54015:18:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2050, this implies that the share of labour in GDP remains constant at today’s
31:765:54093:14:0:102:128:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:level.
32:766:54161:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment impact of increasing State Pension age are based on strong assumptions
32:767:54242:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:as to likely behavioural responses and, as we discuss elsewhere, may either under or
32:768:54326:15:25:90:414:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:over estimate the associated employment impacts of the reform.
32:769:54388:25:15:90:504:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:A major limitation of this analysis is that it can only capture first-round employment
32:770:54474:15:15:90:504:645:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impacts of the proposed reform. The simple modelling used for this analysis does not
32:771:54558:15:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:include any interaction with other economic variables. For example, this excludes
32:772:54639:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:any  second-round  impacts  that  may  result  from  the  increases  in  employment
32:773:54722:15:25:90:311:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:brought about by raising State Pension age.
32:774:54765:25:15:90:504:575:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:To further understand the full impacts of the reform package under analysis here we
32:775:54848:15:15:90:504:560:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:have asked the NIESR to help model the impacts by using NiGEM, their macroeconomic
32:776:54930:15:15:90:504:545:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:model for the UK and world economy. The results of this are discussed further in
32:777:55010:15:37:90:210:530:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Chapter 3 of this paper.
32:778:55034:37:26:90:180:493:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:2.5Results

32:780:55124:15:15:90:504:452:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:fully implemented (i.e. once State Pension age increases to 68 in 2044) range from
32:781:55206:15:15:90:504:437:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:approximately 300,000 under the lower bound estimate to 1.6 million under the
32:782:55283:15:15:90:504:422:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:upper bound estimate. The middle estimate based on an average of these two gives

33:804:56690:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:24
