33:806:56833:15:37:90:466:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working will make it more likely that larger increases in employment occur.
33:807:56908:37:26:90:210:663:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:2.6Sensitivities
33:808:56924:26:15:90:504:637:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The results of this analysis are strongly influenced by the assumptions we have made
33:809:57008:15:15:90:504:622:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and, as we have already outlined, contain a large degree of uncertainty. Here we
33:810:57088:15:25:90:333:607:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:look at the impact of varying these assumptions.
33:811:57136:25:15:90:504:582:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:One of the central assumptions made in producing our main results relates to the
33:812:57216:15:15:90:504:567:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pattern of earnings for older workers. We have assumed that the future pattern of
33:813:57297:15:25:90:347:552:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:total earnings by age remain as they are at present.
33:814:57349:25:15:90:504:527:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In describing the methodology behind our analysis we discussed the information we
33:815:57430:15:15:90:504:512:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:used to arrive at an assumption regarding earnings and how this assumption may
33:816:57508:15:15:90:504:497:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:either over or under estimate the total average earnings of older workers going
33:817:57587:15:15:90:504:482:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:forward. We relax this main assumption regarding the earnings of older worker and
33:818:57668:15:25:90:364:467:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:look at two alternative scenarios of their future trends.
33:819:57725:25:15:90:504:442:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:First we look at the case where total average earnings of those aged 55-69 remain at
33:820:57809:15:15:90:504:427:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the same level of those of younger workers (i.e. show no decline with age). This
33:821:57889:15:15:90:504:412:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:allows us to look at the scenario where the estimates of the future earnings of those
33:822:57974:15:15:90:504:397:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:affected by increases in State Pension age presented in our central results are too
33:823:58057:15:15:90:504:382:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:low. To account for this outcome we assume that average total wages for those
33:824:58134:15:25:90:453:367:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:aged 55-69 do not show any difference from those of younger workers.
33:825:58202:25:15:90:504:342:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Changing this assumption has the greatest impact on the average earnings figure
33:826:58281:15:15:90:504:327:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assumed for the 65-69 age group – under our main assumption the average total
33:827:58358:15:15:90:504:312:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earnings for this group is assumed to be approximately half that of younger workers.
33:828:58442:15:15:90:504:297:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:For the 55-59 and 60-64 age groups a significant difference is discernable but not as
33:829:58527:15:25:90:156:282:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pronounced.
33:830:58538:25:15:90:504:257:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Changing our earnings assumption, therefore, impacts most significantly on our
33:831:58616:15:15:90:504:242:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:lower  bound  estimates.  Under  the  lower  bound  employment  assumption,  only
33:832:58697:15:15:90:504:227:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:those aged 65-69 are affected by the changes and so estimates of GDP impact based
33:833:58778:15:15:90:504:212:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:on the lower bound employment estimates are most sensitive to this change in our
33:834:58858:15:32:90:232:197:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assumptions (see Table 2.4).

35:883:62082:0:110:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:26

35:885:62157:25:15:90:504:686:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The analysis on the likely economic impact of working longer as a result of the
35:886:62236:15:15:90:504:671:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes to State Pension age and associated policies designed to extend working
35:887:62315:15:15:90:504:656:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:life  suggests  a  positive  overall  impact  due  to  the  increased  employment  and
35:888:62401:15:15:90:504:641:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:associated earnings, generated as a result of these reforms. The range of estimates
35:889:62484:15:15:90:504:626:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:should, however, be considered in light of the uncertainty of the likely behavioural
35:890:62568:15:15:90:504:611:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:response  resulting  from  the  State  Pension  age  increases.  The  range  of  results
35:891:62656:15:15:90:504:596:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:presented  in  our  analysis  is  intended  to  reflect  the  uncertainty  surrounding  the
35:892:62747:15:15:90:504:581:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment response. In the analysis, the uncertainty surrounding future trends in
35:893:62829:15:15:90:504:566:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the earnings of older workers is also discussed and sensitivity analysis shows to what
35:894:62915:15:0:90:494:551:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:extent different assumptions on earnings profiles would lead to different results.

36:898:63127:53:25:90:216:432:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.1Introduction
36:899:63142:25:15:90:504:407:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This  chapter  deals  with  the  same  part  of  the  reform  package  discussed  in  the
36:900:63231:15:15:90:504:392:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:previous chapter, the measures to extend working life. In addition, it quantifies the
36:901:63316:15:15:90:504:377:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impact of the introduction of personal accounts. It presents the results of policy
36:902:63398:15:15:90:504:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:simulations with a macroeconomic model of the UK economy. These help to assess
36:903:63476:15:15:90:504:347:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the likely effects of introducing personal accounts and extending working life on a
36:904:63559:15:15:90:504:332:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:number of macroeconomic variables, in particular on output and income, employment
36:905:63640:15:25:90:152:317:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and savings.
36:906:63652:25:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  remainder  of  this  chapter  is  organised  as  follows.  The  next  section  broadly
36:907:63743:15:15:90:504:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:describes the analytical framework and methodology to make clear how they differ
36:908:63823:15:15:90:504:262:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:from the previous chapter and what the underlying assumptions are. It also includes
36:909:63906:15:15:90:504:247:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a discussion of the limitations of a macroeconomic modelling approach. The main
36:910:63985:15:15:90:504:232:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:sections present the results of the introduction of personal accounts and extending
36:911:64068:15:15:90:504:217:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working life and some of the sensitivities around these results. The final section
36:912:64150:15:15:90:504:202:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:concludes by considering whether the results of the two sets of simulations are
36:913:64229:15:37:90:167:187:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:additive or not.
36:914:64245:37:26:90:276:150:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.2Analytical framework
36:915:64268:26:15:90:504:124:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The approach to estimating the economic effects of the reform proposals will be
36:916:64347:15:15:90:504:109:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different from the one followed in the previous chapter. Instead of assessing the
36:917:64428:15:15:90:504:94:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reform package by starting from a partial microeconomic perspective, this chapter
36:918:64509:15:15:90:504:79:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:follows  a  macroeconomic  general  equilibrium  approach.  Such  an  approach  has
36:919:64592:15:15:90:504:64:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:certain advantages and limitations and should, therefore, be seen as complementary
36:920:64674:15:15:90:504:49:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to the results of the previous chapter. In particular, using a macroeconomic model
36:921:64756:15:0:90:504:34:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:makes  it  possible  to  investigate  the  effects  the  reforms  will  have  on  the  wider
37:922:64848:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:28
37:923:64913:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economy, whilst allowing for relevant interactions between economic variables. On
37:924:64994:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the other hand, such an approach by its very nature makes it impossible to identify
37:925:65077:15:37:90:179:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individual effects.
37:926:65096:37:26:90:224:648:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.3Methodology
37:927:65110:26:15:90:504:622:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The DWP asked the NIESR to help model the impact of the reform package by using
37:928:65189:15:25:90:435:607:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:NiGEM, their macroeconomic model for the UK and world economy.
37:929:65251:25:15:90:504:582:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:NiGEM is a large estimated quarterly model of the UK and the world that is intended
37:930:65334:15:15:90:504:567:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to  capture  the  key  features  of  the  economy.  It  is  theoretically  coherent  and
37:931:65422:15:15:90:504:552:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:quantified by means of empirical estimation and calibration over recent historical
37:932:65504:15:15:90:504:537:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:experience.  It  provides  a  plausible  benchmark  for  estimating  the  effects  on  the
37:933:65594:15:25:90:312:522:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:economy of a range of different scenarios.19
37:934:65638:25:15:90:504:497:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is set in what is essentially a New-Keynesian framework where agents are forward
37:935:65721:15:15:90:504:482:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:looking,  but  nominal  rigidities,  namely  sticky  prices  and  adjustment  costs,  slow
37:936:65811:15:15:90:504:467:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:down the adjustment to the long-run equilibrium. It includes complete demand and
37:937:65891:15:15:90:504:452:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:supply sides, as well as extensive monetary and financial sectors. Domestic demand,
37:938:65974:15:15:90:504:437:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:aggregate supply, and the external sector are linked through the wage-price system,
37:939:66057:15:15:90:504:422:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income and wealth, the financial sector, the Government sector, and competitiveness.
37:940:66141:15:15:90:504:407:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The external sector links the UK domestic economy to the rest of the world. The
37:941:66220:15:15:90:504:392:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:theoretical  structure  and  some  simulation  properties  of  NiGEM  are  described  in
37:942:66308:15:15:90:504:377:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Barrell et  al.  (2004).  A  brief  description  of  the  determination  of  savings  and
37:943:66397:15:37:90:413:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:investment within NiGEM is provided in the annex to this report.
37:944:66461:37:26:90:429:325:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.4Limitations and weaknesses in methodology
37:945:66505:26:15:90:504:299:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Using a macroeconomic model such as NiGEM results in a number of limitations. As
37:946:66585:15:25:90:499:284:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:mentioned above, such a model is not well suited to assess effects for individuals.
37:947:66668:25:15:90:504:259:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:A  model  such  as  NiGEM  does,  however,  make  it  possible  to  assess  the  impact
37:948:66755:15:15:90:504:244:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different interventions have on aggregate consumption. Lifetime consumption is, in
37:949:66837:15:15:90:504:229:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:principle, the variable that any Government intervention could be seen to optimise
37:950:66919:15:15:90:505:214:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with its pension policy.20 So one could argue that we should be able to calculate a
37:951:67002:15:15:90:504:199:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Net Present Value (NPV) of the Government’s pension reforms, as in a typical cost-
37:952:67084:15:15:90:504:184:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:benefit analysis such as presented in the Government ‘Green Book’.21 However,
37:953:67161:15:25:90:299:169:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:such a number would not be meaningful.
37:954:67199:25:15:90:504:144:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The main problem with such an approach is that an aggregate only makes sense if it
37:955:67281:15:38:90:504:129:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:has an individual basis. The reason is that in this case it is of crucial importance whose
37:956:67371:38:18:90:505:91:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:19It  is  important  to  note  that  the  specifics  of  the  baseline  are  not  important  in
37:957:67466:18:16:102:353:73:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:generating the simulation results presented here.
37:958:67515:16:21:90:452:57:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:20Or GDP or GNP if we would consider this is an appropriate measure.
37:959:67583:21:0:90:204:36:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:21HM Treasury, 2003.
38:960:67668:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption  is  being  affected  at  what  point  in  time  to  be  able  to  calculate  an
38:961:67760:15:25:90:177:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:appropriate NPV.
38:962:67776:25:15:90:504:675:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:There is also a more general problem with using macroeconomic models such as
38:963:67852:15:15:90:504:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:NiGEM for evaluation purposes. NiGEM is a model that assumes individuals have full
38:964:67934:15:15:90:504:645:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:information,  that  markets  are  perfect  and  the  economic  agents  optimise  their
38:965:68020:15:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:behaviour. In contrast, the pension reform proposals are based on analysis that
38:966:68099:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:suggests  there  are  informational  problems,  pension  markets  are  imperfect,  and
38:967:68185:15:25:90:469:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals do not seem to optimise consumption throughout their lifetime.
38:968:68259:25:15:90:504:575:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The issue of simulating the outcome of pension reforms in a model that reflects
38:969:68338:15:15:90:504:560:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals maximising decisions using the information they have available to them
38:970:68420:15:15:90:504:545:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is addressed directly when we model the impact of increasing State Pension age. As
38:971:68502:15:15:90:504:530:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:part of the modelling exercise, it is assumed that people currently underestimate
38:972:68583:15:15:90:504:515:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their life expectancy and that they will gradually adjust their expectations as time
38:973:68667:15:25:90:459:500:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:goes on. We will address this issue in some more detail in the Section 3.6.
38:974:68742:25:15:90:504:475:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The issue of calculating a NPV of pension reform, in particular personal accounts, will
38:975:68829:15:37:90:219:460:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:be taken up in Chapter 4.
38:976:68854:37:26:90:220:423:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.5Assumptions
38:977:68868:26:15:90:504:397:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:For the purpose of the simulations described in this report, NIESR has constructed a
38:978:68952:15:15:90:504:382:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:new baseline economic scenario for NiGEM that runs until 2059, against which the
38:979:69032:15:15:90:504:367:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impacts of the reform package are modelled. In this way it was possible to ensure
38:980:69113:15:15:90:504:352:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:robust assessment of the impact of the relevant policy interventions proposed in the
38:981:69197:15:15:90:504:337:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:White Paper, Security in retirement: towards a new pensions system (‘the White
38:982:69275:15:15:90:504:322:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Paper’ hereafter), up to 2050. Where possible, NiGEM has used the same assumptions
38:983:69357:15:15:90:504:307:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:as those that were used for the White Paper and in the previous chapter. However,
38:984:69438:15:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:where these assumptions differ, they generally have no significant impact on the
38:985:69518:15:25:90:205:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:results presented here.
38:986:69541:25:15:90:504:252:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As  most  of  the  Government  interventions  considered  are  expected  to  have  an
38:987:69626:15:25:90:471:237:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:impact on consumption, we provide the relevant equation in NiGEM here:22
38:988:69698:25:24:147:326:212:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:C(t) = (    + ρ) * ( HUW(t) + NHW(t)),
38:989:69736:24:15:90:504:188:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:where HUW is human wealth and NHW is financial and housing and asset based
38:990:69810:15:15:90:504:173:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:wealth. The Marginal Propensity to Consume (MPC) is made up of the premium on
38:991:69887:15:15:90:504:158:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the future (     ) and the probability of death (ρ). The higher       and ρ, the less important
38:992:69982:15:25:90:435:143:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is the future, and, therefore, the higher current consumption will be.
38:993:70052:25:15:90:504:118:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As already noted in the introduction, personal accounts are intended to provide a
38:994:70133:15:15:90:504:103:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:new  low-cost  defined  contribution  pension  scheme  for  those  who  do  not  have
38:995:70218:15:32:90:504:88:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:access to an alternative employer scheme that meets certain minimum standards. It
38:996:70299:32:0:90:295:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:22See also Blanchard and Fischer, 1989.
39:997:70338:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:30
39:998:70403:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is estimated that annual contributions will amount to £7-8 billion once the scheme
39:999:70485:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is fully running. However, it is unlikely that all of the contributions into personal
39:1000:70570:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts will be ‘new’ or additional savings, as a number of people will substitute
39:1001:70653:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:away from existing savings once they start contributing to personal accounts. As
39:1002:70733:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:mentioned in the chapter on personal accounts, the Government estimates that
39:1003:70809:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:around 60 per cent of savings in personal accounts will be new savings, resulting in
39:1004:70893:15:25:90:445:625:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:£4-5 billion of additional savings each year due to personal accounts.23
39:1005:70965:25:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:To simulate the introduction of personal accounts in NiGEM, we effectively lowered
39:1006:71047:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  MPC,  a  variable  that  describes  what  proportion  of  income  is  spent  on
39:1007:71131:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption, in the equation that determines consumption behaviour. This implies
39:1008:71211:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that, all else being equal, individuals will save more at every level of income. The
39:1009:71295:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rationale behind this from a modelling point of view is that introducing automatic
39:1010:71377:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:enrolment  and  personal  accounts  will  change  what  could  be  considered  a
39:1011:71457:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:sub-optimally high MPC. This change in the MPC would be the result of overcoming
39:1012:71537:15:15:90:504:495:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:some of the underlying psychological barriers to saving, such as inertia and myopia,
39:1013:71621:15:15:90:504:480:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:whilst providing a new simple low-cost savings vehicle to invest pension contributions
39:1014:71707:15:30:90:142:465:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:efficiently.
39:1015:71719:30:26:90:312:435:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.6Personal accounts – results
39:1016:71749:26:15:90:504:409:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Following the proposals in the White Paper, it is assumed that personal accounts will
39:1017:71834:15:15:90:504:394:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:be introduced in 2012 and that there will be a phasing-in period of three years. In
39:1018:71917:15:15:90:504:379:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:line with the estimate presented above, we have simulated a total savings increase
39:1019:71999:15:15:90:504:364:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of  £4.5  billion  in  our  central  scenario.24  Figure  3.1  shows  what  happens  to  the
39:1020:72091:15:15:90:504:349:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal savings rate (as a percentage of disposable income) in the central scenario.
39:1021:72176:15:15:90:504:334:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:From 2012 the savings rate increases quickly in the first three years, in line with the
39:1022:72263:15:15:90:505:319:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:phasing-in.25 After this it settles around 0.5 percentage point above the base case
39:1023:72346:15:43:90:417:304:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:until the end of the forecasting period presented here, in 2050.26
39:1024:72412:43:19:90:505:261:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:23See  Regulatory  impact  assessment  to  the  White  Paper  Security  in  retirement:
39:1025:72499:19:16:102:429:242:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:towards a new pensions system, 2006, and Hawksworth, 2006.
39:1026:72557:16:18:90:505:226:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:24In 2006 earnings terms, i.e. the nominal numbers will be significantly higher in
39:1027:72639:18:16:102:445:208:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2012 and onwards as they are uprated by economy-wide earnings.
39:1028:72701:16:19:90:505:192:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:25As is clear from the graph, the savings rates also move marginally in the run-up
39:1029:72783:19:14:102:505:173:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to 2012; this has no direct connection with personal accounts, but is the result
39:1030:72863:14:14:102:505:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of  endogenous  changes  in  the  model  that  result  from  economic  agents
39:1031:72940:14:17:102:294:145:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:anticipating the introduction in 2012.
39:1032:72978:17:18:90:505:128:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:26As noted, the MPC in NiGEM is changed permanently to simulate the possible
39:1033:73054:18:14:102:505:110:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:impact of personal accounts. This is based on the premise that personal accounts
39:1034:73134:14:15:102:505:96:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:will  be  instrumental  in  permanently  raising  the  personal  savings  rate,  as  was
39:1035:73222:15:14:102:505:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:supported by the evidence presented in Hawksworth, 2006. In practice, it might
39:1036:73300:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:be that, whatever the initial offset, there will be stronger (or weaker) substitution
39:1037:73385:14:0:102:227:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects throughout time.
40:1038:73474:0:14:90:459:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.1Impact of personal accounts on saving – central
40:1039:73531:14:295:175:225:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:scenario
40:1040:73539:295:15:90:504:407:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The savings increase associated with the introduction of personal accounts implies
40:1041:73621:15:15:90:504:392:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:lower  consumption  in  the  short-term,  which  initially  has  a  downward  effect  on
40:1042:73709:15:15:90:504:377:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic activity. Figure 3.2 plots the path that two different measures of economic
40:1043:73793:15:15:90:504:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:activity, GDP and GNP are forecast to follow between now and 2050 compared to
40:1044:73870:15:15:90:504:347:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the base case. GDP represents annual domestic production, whereas GNP also takes
40:1045:73950:15:25:90:333:332:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:into account (net) income received from abroad.
40:1046:73997:25:15:90:504:307:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Looking at GDP, the most commonly used indicator of economic activity, the graph
40:1047:74077:15:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:shows a very small increase in economic activity between now and 2012.27 This has
40:1048:74158:15:15:90:504:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to do with the fact that individuals and financial markets are assumed to be forward
40:1049:74242:15:15:90:504:262:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:looking. Financial markets anticipate that future monetary policy will react to lower
40:1050:74327:15:15:90:504:247:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption  by  lowering  interest  rates.  As  a  result  exchange  rates  will  react
40:1051:74415:15:15:90:504:232:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:immediately and will ‘jump’ down to a new equilibrium. In turn, the lower exchange
40:1052:74497:15:25:90:490:217:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rate causes exports to rise, which results in a small increase in economic activity.
40:1053:74581:25:15:90:504:192:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The small decrease in GDP compared to the baseline from 2012 onwards is caused
40:1054:74659:15:34:90:504:177:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:by the initial savings increase, which results in lower consumption in the short run.
40:1055:74744:34:18:90:505:143:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:27It is important to keep in mind that here and in the remainder of this chapter any
40:1056:74828:18:15:102:505:125:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects are (level) differences compared to the base case. When economic activity
40:1057:74909:15:14:102:505:110:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is concerned, this base case forecasts an average long-term growth rate of around
40:1058:74990:14:15:102:505:96:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2¼ per cent. Therefore, if one would want to find the growth rate in any particular
40:1059:75073:15:14:102:504:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:year one should roughly add 2¼ per cent to the (level) difference in that particular
40:1060:75157:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:year and the previous year. For all scenarios concerned this implies that annual
40:1061:75237:14:0:102:351:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:growth rates are always projected to be positive.
41:1062:75351:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The economy then gradually reverts back to the original growth path as it adjusts to
41:1063:75435:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the new level of savings in the economy. It should be emphasised that all of the
41:1064:75515:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes  described  here  are  very  small.  For  example,  the  cumulative  downward
41:1065:75600:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effect  does  not  go  beyond  0.15  per  cent,  and  the  largest  impact  on  economic
41:1066:75688:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:growth in any given year remains below 0.05 per cent, a magnitude that is not likely
41:1067:75772:15:33:90:230:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to be detectable in practice.
41:1068:75801:33:14:90:479:607:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.2Impact of personal accounts on economic activity –
41:1069:75861:14:284:175:270:593:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:central scenario
41:1070:75877:284:15:90:504:309:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is immediately clear from comparing the paths of GDP and GNP that they produce
41:1071:75958:15:15:90:504:294:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a very similar pattern. The main difference between the two is that GNP is higher at
41:1072:76042:15:15:90:504:279:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:any point in time; it settles around 0.2 per cent above the base case, still representing
41:1073:76131:15:25:90:168:264:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a limited effect.
41:1074:76148:25:15:90:504:239:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The reason that GNP is higher than GDP in this scenario has to do with the fact that
41:1075:76232:15:15:90:504:224:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:it includes investment income received from abroad. NiGEM models the UK as a
41:1076:76308:15:15:90:504:209:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:small open economy in which investment decisions are taken independently from
41:1077:76385:15:15:90:504:194:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the domestic savings decisions. If, as in this case, the domestic supply of savings
41:1078:76468:15:15:90:504:179:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increases without a fundamental change in the profitability of investment, most of
41:1079:76550:15:15:90:504:164:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:these savings will go abroad. This in turn leads to a build-up of foreign capital. The
41:1080:76636:15:15:90:504:149:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:associated investment returns that flow back do not show up in the GDP measure of
41:1081:76717:15:34:90:312:134:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:economic activity but are reflected in GNP.28
41:1082:76762:34:19:90:505:100:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:28As  an  aggregate  model,  NiGEM  is  not  designed  to  describe  the  investment
41:1083:76846:19:14:102:505:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:allocation  of  personal  accounts.  The  overall  portfolio  of  the  economy  has  to
41:1084:76933:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:adjust to contain more foreign assets, even if personal accounts do not, and in
41:1085:77012:14:15:102:505:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:competitive  financial  system  this  process  takes  place  through  very  minor
41:1086:77093:15:0:102:219:38:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:adjustments in returns.
42:1087:77181:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Given the inherent uncertainty around participation rates and the exact level of
42:1088:77261:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:additional savings, we have modelled two additional scenarios which, together with
42:1089:77343:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:our  central  scenario,  should  provide  a  realistic  range  of  outcomes  in  terms  of
42:1090:77433:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:additional  savings.  The  conservative  and  optimistic  scenarios  model  additional
42:1091:77519:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:savings of respectively £2.5 and £7 billion.29 The results of these analyses show the
42:1092:77604:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:same patterns in savings behaviour and economic activity as the central scenario.
42:1093:77685:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The long-term effect on GDP is again close to zero, whereas the long-term effect on
42:1094:77768:15:37:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:GNP is 0.1 and 0.3 per cent respectively in the conservative and optimistic scenarios.
42:1095:77854:37:26:90:344:573:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.7Personal accounts – sensitivities
42:1096:77890:26:15:90:504:547:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As noted above, NiGEM is a model that assumes all economic actors are forward
42:1097:77967:15:15:90:504:532:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:looking, i.e. they adjust their behaviour today to events which they know will occur
42:1098:78051:15:15:90:504:517:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in the future, though there are some frictions in the adjustment process. To test how
42:1099:78136:15:15:90:504:502:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:sensitive the results are to this assumption, the scenarios were also run in a model
42:1100:78220:15:15:90:504:487:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with  financial  markets,  wages,  business  investment  and  consumers  who  are  all
42:1101:78306:15:15:90:504:472:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:backward  looking,  in  that  reactions  depend  only  on  past  events  and  not
42:1102:78387:15:25:90:224:457:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expectations of the future.
42:1103:78414:25:15:90:504:432:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Unsurprisingly,  the  economy  shows  more  of  a  cycle  with  backward  looking
42:1104:78495:15:15:90:504:417:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:behaviour, as everybody acts as if they are totally surprised by the policy change.
42:1105:78578:15:15:90:504:402:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:However, even with backward looking agents, the short-term effect on GDP is still
42:1106:78659:15:15:90:504:387:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:relatively small (Figure 3.3). If only consumers are backward looking, the impact is
42:1107:78743:15:15:90:504:372:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:roughly the same as in the case with forward looking consumers. If other economic
42:1108:78824:15:15:90:504:357:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:agents, i.e. financial markets and businesses selling goods to consumers, are also
42:1109:78906:15:15:90:504:342:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:surprised by the new policy, the cumulative downward effect on output is magnified
42:1110:78988:15:15:90:504:327:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:about threefold. Compared to forward looking agents, there is also more of an
42:1111:79065:15:15:90:504:312:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:upswing after the initial shock, resulting in a cumulative positive effect for a number
42:1112:79152:15:15:90:504:297:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of years after 2023, with a peak just around 0.25 per cent in 2032, after which GDP
42:1113:79235:15:226:90:356:282:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:gradually falls again in the direction of the base case.
42:1114:79291:226:0:90:248:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:29As before, in 2006 earnings.
43:1115:79386:0:14:90:463:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.3Impact of personal accounts on GDP – backward
43:1116:79441:14:283:175:408:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:looking behaviour by economic agents
43:1117:79477:283:25:90:342:419:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.8Extending working life – results
43:1118:79512:25:15:90:504:394:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The introduction presented the rationale for working longer in a society in which
43:1119:79593:15:15:90:504:379:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people on average live substantially longer than before. In the pension context, the
43:1120:79677:15:15:90:504:364:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:most important measure to extend working life is the increase of the State Pension
43:1121:79759:15:25:90:112:349:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:age.
43:1122:79763:25:15:90:504:324:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  previous  chapter,  dealing  with  increasing  State  Pension  age  and  extending
43:1123:79850:15:15:90:504:309:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working life, explains how raising State Pension age might increase employment in
43:1124:79931:15:15:90:504:294:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a number of ways. If some people retire too early due to information failures then
43:1125:80013:15:15:90:504:279:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increasing State Pension age may help to overcome this by signalling to them that
43:1126:80094:15:15:90:504:264:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:they need to work longer than they otherwise thought. The reduction in income
43:1127:80171:15:25:90:496:249:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:from later access to a State Pension may also result in individuals working longer.
43:1128:80254:25:15:90:504:224:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As  the  Government  proposals  see  State  Pension  age  for  both  men  and  women
43:1129:80338:15:15:90:504:209:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:gradually  increase  by  three  years  –  from  65  to  6830  –  we  have  modelled  that
43:1130:80427:15:15:90:504:194:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals adjust their estimates of their life expectancy by three years as well as a
43:1131:80514:15:15:90:504:179:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:result of the reform package. In other words, we have assumed that individuals see
43:1132:80596:15:15:90:504:164:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:an increase in State Pension age as a signal that their life expectancy has increased by
43:1133:80684:15:15:90:504:149:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the same amount. This might seem a somewhat simplistic behavioural assumption
43:1134:80761:15:15:90:504:134:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:at first, as we actually estimate life expectancy to increase by more than three years
43:1135:80847:15:15:90:504:119:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:between  now  and  2050,  but  fits  with  a  world  of  imperfect  information  and
43:1136:80931:15:24:90:504:104:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals  that  can  be  considered  having  a  bounded  rationality.31  As  a  result,
43:1137:81021:24:19:90:505:80:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:30That  is,  after  the  equalisation  of  retirement  ages  for  men  and  women  to  65
43:1138:81110:19:16:102:233:61:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:between 2010 and 2020.
43:1139:81132:16:0:90:286:45:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:31See, for example, Kahneman, 2003.
44:1140:81232:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals change their behaviour infrequently and often use rules of thumb to
44:1141:81311:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:drive their behaviour. It is assumed that the adjustment of life expectancy is a gradual
44:1142:81399:15:25:90:311:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:process that will take ten years to complete.
44:1143:81444:25:15:90:504:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The available evidence clearly suggests that most individuals do underestimate their
44:1144:81528:15:15:90:504:645:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:life expectancy, but that this declines with age. As is clear from Figure 3.4, even
44:1145:81611:15:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:those close to retirement on average appear to underestimate their life expectancy
44:1146:81693:15:33:90:469:615:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:by more than three years, which makes our assumption a reasonable one.32
44:1147:81765:33:482:90:487:582:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.4Individual underestimates of life expectancy, by age
44:1148:81827:482:19:90:505:100:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:32The findings presented in Figure 3.4 are reproduced from the second report of
44:1149:81906:19:14:102:505:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the Pensions Commission, 2005, p. 93. In Appendix D the report also presents
44:1150:81982:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:evidence from a National Statistics Omnibus survey, which confirms the findings
44:1151:82061:14:0:102:284:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of O’Brien, Fenn and Diacon, 2005.
45:1152:82160:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Figure 3.5 shows the increase in the level of employment in the central scenario,
45:1153:82241:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which leads to about 900,000 extra workers by 2050, equivalent to an increase of
45:1154:82321:15:15:90:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2.7 per cent.33 The underlying increase in labour supply is the same one that was
45:1155:82402:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:used  for  the  central  scenario  in  the  previous  chapter;  however,  the  increase  in
45:1156:82493:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:percentage terms differs slightly as NiGEM has its own labour market baseline that
45:1157:82575:15:33:90:454:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:shows marginal differences compared to the baseline used in Chapter 2.
45:1158:82645:33:14:90:466:607:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.5Impact of longer working and life expectancy on
45:1159:82702:14:284:175:252:593:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:employment
45:1160:82712:284:15:90:504:309:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Figure 3.6 shows that extending working life has a substantial impact on economic
45:1161:82793:15:15:90:504:294:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:activity, particularly if we compare it to the effect of introducing personal accounts.
45:1162:82880:15:15:90:504:279:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:GDP roughly rises in line with the increase in labour supply. However, the increase is
45:1163:82966:15:15:90:504:264:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:not one-for-one, which has to do with the fact that the employment increase does
45:1164:83046:15:15:90:504:249:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:not take account of the effective hours worked. As it is assumed that the additional
45:1165:83130:15:77:90:504:234:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:workers  on  average  will  work  fewer  hours  than  the  rest  of  the  working  age
45:1166:83216:77:18:90:505:157:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:33The graph shows some slight variation in employment in the run-up to the first
45:1167:83296:18:14:102:505:139:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:change in State Pension age in 2026. This has to do with the extra savings that
45:1168:83375:14:15:102:505:125:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:result from individuals adjusting their life expectancy. A fall in consumption that
45:1169:83458:15:14:102:505:110:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:follows form a change in the perception of the length of life and a reorientation
45:1170:83539:14:15:102:504:96:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of production to exports may cause a slight reduction in the level of demand and
45:1171:83619:15:14:102:505:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment  as  the  economy  adjusts.  The  more  forward  looking  the  wage
45:1172:83697:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:bargaining  process  is,  the  smaller  the  impact  on  output  will  be  when  savings
45:1173:83785:14:0:102:449:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rise. See Barrell and Dury, 2003, for further discussion on this point.
46:1174:83921:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:population, the effect on GDP will be correspondingly smaller. In this scenario, it is
46:1175:84007:15:25:90:472:700:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:estimated that GDP will be 1.7 per cent higher than the base case in 2050.34
46:1176:84083:25:15:90:504:675:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The impact of 1.7 per cent is higher than the 1.4 per cent in the central scenario of
46:1177:84168:15:15:90:504:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the previous chapter. This is partly explained by the fact that we are now introducing
46:1178:84254:15:15:90:504:645:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the labour supply changes in a fully specified model that takes account of relevant
46:1179:84337:15:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:interactions of economic variables. However, one underlying assumption in NiGEM
46:1180:84416:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is also a relevant driver behind the result: NiGEM assumes that all labour supply is
46:1181:84500:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:equally productive. In contrast, the previous chapter assumed that the additional
46:1182:84581:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:labour supply would earn lower wages – i.e. be less productive – than the rest of the
46:1183:84666:15:33:90:140:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economy.
46:1184:84674:33:14:90:503:537:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.6Impact of longer working and adjusted life expectancy
46:1185:84737:14:395:175:299:523:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:on economic activity
46:1186:84757:395:18:90:505:128:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:34Older workers work fewer hours. This simulation used the same assumption on
46:1187:84834:18:14:102:505:110:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:hours worked as the previous chapter, 74 per cent. This implies that the effective
46:1188:84916:14:15:102:505:96:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increase in employment was 2.0 per cent. The main reason the GDP impact of
46:1189:84990:15:14:102:505:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:1.7 per cent is slightly lower has to due with the fact that not all economy wide
46:1190:85071:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:investments tend to move in line with changes in employment (e.g. Government
46:1191:85147:14:0:102:165:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:investment).
47:1192:85224:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is interesting to note what happens with the savings rate. Figure 3.7 shows a
47:1193:85304:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:substantial increase in the savings rate. As a result of the adjustment of their life
47:1194:85389:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expectancy, individuals realise they will have a longer retirement than previously
47:1195:85471:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expected. If they do not adjust their behaviour, they will end up with lower incomes
47:1196:85555:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in retirement than desired. As part of our simulation, we assume that people will
47:1197:85636:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:work longer to make up for this potential shortfall. The result of our modelling
47:1198:85716:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:exercise shows that the increase in the length of the average working life that we
47:1199:85798:15:15:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:have modelled is not sufficient to bring income in retirement up to the desired level,
47:1200:85884:15:25:90:403:595:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:but that savings during working life will be increased as well.35
47:1201:85949:25:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The increase in savings associated with the upward adjustment of life expectancy
47:1202:86029:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:explains why the increase in GNP (2.0 per cent) is higher than that of GDP (1.7 per
47:1203:86112:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:cent), as part of the savings will be invested abroad. However, the difference is
47:1204:86193:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:limited to 0.3 percentage point because there is also a higher domestic demand for
47:1205:86275:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:savings. This is the result of the increased labour supply, which in turn will lead to a
47:1206:86363:15:25:90:496:495:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:higher demand for capital as the extra labour supply is absorbed in the economy.
47:1207:86443:25:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:There is uncertainty about the size of the impact of increasing State Pension age on
47:1208:86527:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:labour supply and thus on the economy as a whole. We have, therefore, also done
47:1209:86606:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:simulations using a smaller and larger labour market impact36. For these simulations,
47:1210:86691:15:15:90:504:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:we have used the same assumptions as those of the previous chapter. In the ‘low
47:1211:86770:15:15:90:504:410:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:participation’ scenario this leads to about 0.3 million additional workers in 2050,
47:1212:86853:15:25:90:485:395:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with the number for the ‘high participation’ scenario being around 1.6 million.
47:1213:86932:25:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The two scenarios show broadly the same pattern in employment, GDP and GNP.
47:1214:87007:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The main difference is that the savings rate in the ‘high’ scenario shows more of a
47:1215:87090:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:decline  towards  the  end  of  the  simulation  period.  This  is  due  to  the  ‘trade-off’
47:1216:87183:15:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:between  longer  working  and  higher  saving  as  a  means  to  increase  retirement
47:1217:87268:15:15:90:504:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income; the high participation scenario implies that individuals have to save less to
47:1218:87353:15:15:90:504:295:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reach  their  desired  replacement  rate  in  retirement.  As  a  result,  the  difference
47:1219:87443:15:15:90:504:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:between GDP and GNP is smaller in the high participation scenario. The GDP impact
47:1220:87524:15:15:90:504:265:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in  2050  in  the  high  and  low  participation  scenario  is  2.9  and  0.4  per  cent
47:1221:87612:15:44:90:504:250:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:respectively. The corresponding GNP impacts are 3.1 and 0.9 per cent respectively.
47:1222:87694:44:18:90:505:206:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:35If forward looking individuals know that they will be working longer, but do not
47:1223:87776:18:15:102:504:188:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expect to die any later then their need for savings to use in their (shorter) retirement
47:1224:87864:15:14:102:505:173:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is reduced, and hence they may save less as soon as they decide to work longer.
47:1225:87943:14:14:102:505:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This  may  indeed  be  why  US  citizens,  who  work  significantly  longer  than  UK
47:1226:88028:14:15:102:505:145:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:citizens, save less, as Sefton and Kirsanova, 2006, discuss. Given that the model
47:1227:88109:15:14:102:505:130:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:has  forward  looking  consumers,  without  modelling  an  adjustment  of  life
47:1228:88188:14:15:102:505:116:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expectancy,  NiGEM  would  show  a  decrease  in  savings  as  a  result  of  imposed
47:1229:88273:15:14:102:505:101:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:longer working lives, as optimising agents that work longer would need to put
47:1230:88350:14:16:102:385:87:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:less money aside to get the same income in retirement.
47:1231:88404:16:18:90:505:71:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:36The change in the expected life expectancy – three years – remains the same for
47:1232:88485:18:0:102:167:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:all scenarios.
48:1233:88501:0:14:90:487:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.7Savings impacts of longer working and adjusted life
48:1234:88562:14:307:175:243:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:expectancy
48:1235:88572:307:26:90:374:395:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.9Extending working life – sensitivities
48:1236:88613:26:15:90:504:369:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:To assess how sensitive our results are to the modelling assumption of forward
48:1237:88691:15:15:90:504:354:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:looking economic agents, we have also run a number of scenarios with backward
48:1238:88768:15:15:90:504:339:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:looking consumers and backward looking financial, labour and investment markets.
48:1239:88848:15:15:90:504:324:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:If  only  consumers  are  backward  looking,  i.e.  they  act  as  if  they  are  completely
48:1240:88940:15:15:90:504:309:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:surprised by the changes in State Pension age, the GDP effects are very similar to
48:1241:89022:15:15:90:504:294:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:those shown above.37 If not only consumers, but also other economic agents behave
48:1242:89103:15:194:90:502:279:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in a backward looking fashion, effects differ and are more cyclical (see Figure 3.8).
48:1243:89188:194:18:90:505:85:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:37However,  it  is  perhaps  difficult  to  imagine  a  scenario  in  which  individuals  are
48:1244:89281:18:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:completely surprised by the changes in State Pension age, whilst at the same
48:1245:89357:14:15:102:505:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:time we consider them ‘forward looking’ enough to adjust their life expectancy
48:1246:89435:15:0:102:205:38:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and act accordingly.
49:1247:89520:0:14:90:503:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.8Impact of longer working and adjusted life expectancy
49:1248:89583:14:14:175:502:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:on economic activity – backward looking behaviour by
49:1249:89635:14:322:175:276:688:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:economic agents
49:1250:89650:322:26:90:402:366:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.10Modelling the different parts together
49:1251:89692:26:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Our final scenario puts the two parts of the reform package together. Figures 3.9
49:1252:89773:15:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and 3.10 show what happens to savings and economic activity if we assume that we
49:1253:89853:15:15:90:504:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:can add together the two policies described in the previous sections. This exercise
49:1254:89936:15:15:90:504:295:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:shows that personal savings rates would increase by about 1.5 percentage points,
49:1255:90016:15:15:90:504:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:roughly the same as the sum of the separate increases. This higher savings rate is
49:1256:90098:15:15:90:504:265:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reflected in a higher GNP, which is 2.3 per cent higher than the base case in 2050. On
49:1257:90184:15:15:90:504:250:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the other hand, GDP and employment are roughly the same as in the scenarios
49:1258:90259:15:15:90:504:235:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:presented  in  the  section  on  longer  working,  as  the  introduction  of  personal
49:1259:90345:15:25:90:426:220:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts is unlikely to have a substantial impact on these variables.
49:1260:90414:25:15:90:504:195:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:One can debate whether the impacts of personal accounts and extending working
49:1261:90491:15:15:90:504:180:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:life should be assessed jointly or not. Contrary to the simulations we have presented
49:1262:90576:15:15:90:504:165:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:here, personal accounts could be seen as the vehicle that people will use when they
49:1263:90659:15:15:90:504:150:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:adjust their savings as they become more aware of the fact that they will live much
49:1264:90742:15:15:90:504:135:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:longer than previously anticipated. This seems a realistic assumption, as personal
49:1265:90824:15:15:90:504:120:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts are primarily set up to help those who are currently under-saving. The
49:1266:90903:15:15:90:504:105:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reason for this under-saving is of secondary importance. It is likely that there are
49:1267:90987:15:15:90:504:90:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:multiple  reasons  for  this.  In  practice,  both  the  behavioural  barriers  that  were
49:1268:91077:15:15:90:504:75:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:mentioned in the paragraphs on personal accounts and the adjustment of expectations
49:1269:91160:15:15:90:504:60:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that  were  modelled  in  the  sections  on  longer  working,  are  likely  to  be  relevant
49:1270:91252:15:0:90:504:45:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:factors. However, as the size of the savings increase in the longer working scenarios
50:1271:91402:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is  already  much  larger  than  that  in  personal  accounts,  it  seems  unlikely  that  in
50:1272:91495:15:33:90:482:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:practice there will be a savings impact as large as the one shown in Figure 3.9.
50:1273:91575:33:14:90:492:667:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.9Joint savings impact of personal accounts and longer
50:1274:91637:14:0:175:406:653:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:working with adjusted life expectancy
51:1275:91739:0:14:91:503:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 3.10Joint impact on economic activity of personal accounts
51:1276:91804:14:273:176:475:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:and longer working with adjusted life expectancy
51:1277:91852:273:25:91:223:429:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:3.11Conclusion
51:1278:91866:25:15:91:505:404:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This chapter has assessed the macroeconomic impact of two major parts of the
51:1279:91942:15:15:91:505:389:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reform, the introduction of personal accounts and increasing State Pension age
51:1280:92020:15:15:91:505:374:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which  is  expected  to  extend  working  lives.  The  results  show  that  the  impact  of
51:1281:92111:15:15:91:505:359:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal  accounts  is  mainly  on  incomes  (as  reflected  in  GNP)  and  is  small  but
51:1282:92201:15:15:91:505:344:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:positive. In our central scenario, incomes are 0.2 per cent higher in the long-term.
51:1283:92285:15:15:91:505:329:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The impact of longer working is both on GDP and incomes and is estimated to be
51:1284:92363:15:15:91:505:314:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:substantially larger. In our central scenario, GDP increases by 1.7 per cent, with
51:1285:92445:15:25:91:267:299:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:incomes being 2.0 per cent higher.
51:1286:92479:25:15:91:505:274:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Both sets of simulations were subjected to alternative scenarios and sensitivities. The
51:1287:92566:15:15:91:505:259:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:alternative scenarios show a relatively wide range of possible impacts, but they all
51:1288:92650:15:15:91:505:244:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:remain  clearly  positive.  Our  sensitivity  analysis  has  mainly  focused  on  when
51:1289:92736:15:15:91:505:229:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic agents (i.e. consumers, businesses) incorporate knowledge of the new
51:1290:92813:15:15:91:505:214:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:policies into their behaviour. If economic agents act as if they have absolutely no
51:1291:92896:15:15:91:505:199:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:prior knowledge, the short-term effects tend to be amplified, though long-term
51:1292:92974:15:15:91:505:184:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects tend to be roughly the same as in the case when economic agents anticipate
51:1293:93056:15:25:91:176:169:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the new policies.
51:1294:93073:25:15:91:505:144:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The final section showed what would happen if the effects of the two sets of policies
51:1295:93158:15:15:91:505:129:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:were additive. It was argued that in practice this would not be wholly the case, as
51:1296:93241:15:15:91:505:114:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts would likely be an important vehicle for the additional savings
51:1297:93322:15:0:91:489:99:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that would result from individuals adjusting their life expectancy by three years.
52:1298:93538:0:242:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
52:1299:93555:242:39:90:409:562:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:4   Estimating the social
52:1300:93580:39:38:133:369:523:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:welfare impact of
52:1301:93597:38:39:133:464:485:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:consumption smoothing
52:1302:93618:39:52:133:494:446:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:through personal accounts
52:1303:93643:52:25:90:216:394:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.1Introduction
52:1304:93658:25:15:90:504:369:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The introduction of personal accounts, automatic enrolment and minimum employer
52:1305:93737:15:15:90:504:354:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contributions (as outlined in the Introduction) will have a significant impact on those
52:1306:93824:15:15:90:504:339:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:who are currently not saving for retirement, but who will be once the reforms are
52:1307:93905:15:15:90:504:324:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:introduced. This may be a self-evident fact; however the purpose of this chapter is to
52:1308:93991:15:15:90:504:309:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:focus on these people and explore a method which allows us to quantify the size of
52:1309:94073:15:25:90:395:294:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the social welfare gain produced by these particular reforms.
52:1310:94134:25:15:90:504:269:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:However, we do not estimate the social welfare impacts of longer working lives, as
52:1311:94216:15:15:90:504:254:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:this would require developing a model to take account of individual preferences
52:1312:94295:15:15:90:504:239:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:amongst those affected by the change. This would involve estimating the losses or
52:1313:94376:15:15:90:504:224:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:(non-financial) gains individuals derive directly from working. There is no consensus
52:1314:94461:15:15:90:504:209:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:as to the disutility of work and to create a model to estimate it would be beyond the
52:1315:94546:15:15:90:504:194:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:scope  of  this  paper.  Neither  do  we  estimate  the  welfare  impacts  of  the  overall
52:1316:94637:15:15:90:504:179:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increases in the size of the economy as a result of the changes in State Pension age
52:1317:94721:15:15:90:504:164:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and  increases  in  pension  saving.  The  reason  we  focus  on  the  introduction  of
52:1318:94808:15:15:90:504:149:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts in this chapter is that it is a relatively simple example to use to
52:1319:94893:15:0:90:423:134:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:explore how social welfare impacts of reforms could be measured.
53:1320:95028:0:93:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
53:1321:95045:93:25:90:276:711:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.2Analytical framework
53:1322:95068:25:15:90:504:686:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Saving for retirement is central to the economic concept of consumption smoothing
53:1323:95149:15:15:90:504:671:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and, therefore, to maximising wellbeing throughout life. Individuals have varying
53:1324:95230:15:15:90:504:656:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:levels  of  income  in  different  periods  of  their  life.  For  example,  the  majority  of
53:1325:95324:15:15:90:504:641:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals in full-time education generally have low incomes and jobs earlier in life
53:1326:95410:15:15:90:504:626:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:are likely to generate smaller incomes than those later in someone’s career. Most
53:1327:95491:15:15:90:504:611:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people’s  consumption,  however,  does  not  follow  this  income  pattern  exactly;
53:1328:95575:15:15:90:504:596:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:broadly speaking most individuals borrow when they are younger and on relatively
53:1329:95655:15:15:90:504:581:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:low incomes and save throughout their working life to ensure a higher standard of
53:1330:95736:15:15:90:504:566:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:living in retirement than that afforded by their State Pension entitlement only. This
53:1331:95821:15:15:90:504:551:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:concept  implies  that  there  is  a  benefit  in  transferring  income  from  periods  of
53:1332:95911:15:15:90:504:536:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:relatively high to those of relatively low income, in other words to smooth income
53:1333:95993:15:15:90:504:521:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:over  an  individual’s  lifecycle  through  saving  and  thus  facilitating  consumption
53:1334:96081:15:25:90:148:506:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:smoothing.
53:1335:96091:25:15:90:504:481:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Current pension saving behaviour does not conform to the conditions required to
53:1336:96170:15:15:90:504:466:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:have optimal outcomes in terms of consumption smoothing throughout life: there
53:1337:96248:15:15:90:505:451:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f9:are both demand and supply problems. In Security in Retirement: towards a new
53:1338:96325:15:15:90:504:436:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:pension system38, the White Paper published in May 2006, it was estimated that at
53:1339:96406:15:15:90:504:421:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:least seven million people are under-saving for retirement. This means that their
53:1340:96487:15:15:90:504:406:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:current savings behaviour and wealth holdings are such that they are at risk of a
53:1341:96568:15:15:90:504:391:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:significant  fall  in  living  standards  at  retirement  and  they  are  not  smoothing
53:1342:96656:15:15:90:504:376:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption in a way to maximise utility over their lifetimes. There are a number of
53:1343:96740:15:15:90:504:361:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different reasons why demand and supply do not live up to the perfect economic
53:1344:96818:15:22:90:286:346:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:standard as set out in the introduction:
53:1345:96858:22:15:90:504:324:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Informational problems: there is widespread evidence that people have only a
53:1346:96937:15:15:102:505:309:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:limited understanding of pension issues. For example, a survey carried out on
53:1347:97014:15:15:102:505:294:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:behalf of the Pensions Commission in 2005 found that 20 per cent of people
53:1348:97088:15:15:102:504:279:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:felt that they knew little or nothing about pension issues.39 On National Pensions
53:1349:97170:15:15:102:505:264:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Day in March 2006 over 1000 people across the UK debated pension reform. At
53:1350:97245:15:15:102:505:249:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the start of the debate only 13 per cent of participants agreed with the statement
53:1351:97327:15:15:102:505:234:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:‘I know a lot about pensions.’ Even if individuals did understand the basics, it is
53:1352:97410:15:15:102:505:219:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:highly complex to work out how much they should be saving in pensions, or
53:1353:97483:15:127:102:418:204:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:other products, or to make detailed asset allocation decisions.
53:1354:97546:127:21:90:164:77:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:38DWP, 2006.
53:1355:97558:21:0:90:249:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:39Pensions Commission, 2005.
54:1356:97657:0:89:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
54:1357:97674:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Behavioural economics suggests that there are inherent barriers for individuals
54:1358:97756:15:15:102:505:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to save optimally even if the informational barriers were overcome. Inertia and
54:1359:97835:15:15:102:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:procrastination mean that individuals, even when they understand pensions and
54:1360:97912:15:15:102:505:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:realise that they need to be saving, find it hard to begin to save. Myopia means
54:1361:97992:15:15:102:505:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that people are short-sighted, and are unable to clearly see the needs of their
54:1362:98071:15:15:102:505:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:future  self.  Even  though  they  would  like  to  save,  current  spending  pressures
54:1363:98158:15:15:102:505:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:often seem more important than saving for the future. In economic terms, this
54:1364:98235:15:15:102:505:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:implies that individuals have higher discount rates of future benefits the closer
54:1365:98316:15:15:102:505:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:they get to the point of receiving the benefit (e.g. hyperbolic discount rates).
54:1366:98396:15:15:102:505:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Individuals also fail to review savings behaviour over time and fail to account for
54:1367:98479:15:15:102:505:565:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:changes in circumstances, such as increases in life expectancy, changes in rates
54:1368:98559:15:22:102:211:550:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of return or earnings.
54:1369:98581:22:15:90:504:528:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The  problems  on  the  demand  side  for  pensions  also  create  problems  on  the
54:1370:98668:15:15:102:505:513:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:supply  side.  Firstly,  the  tendency  of  individuals  to  underestimate  their  future
54:1371:98757:15:15:102:505:498:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:needs  as  well  as  to  delay  relatively  complex  decisions,  individuals  need  to  be
54:1372:98847:15:15:102:505:483:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:actively persuaded by providers of the need to have a pension on an individual
54:1373:98925:15:15:102:505:468:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:basis. This is particularly true when their employers are disengaged from pension
54:1374:99006:15:15:102:505:453:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:provision. Secondly the complexity of pension products means that individuals
54:1375:99083:15:15:102:505:438:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:need to be protected by regulation that prevents misselling of pensions. Both of
54:1376:99163:15:15:102:505:423:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:these issues make the process of selling a pension expensive which leads to high
54:1377:99243:15:15:102:505:408:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:annual  management  charges  to  recoup  the  costs  to  the  provider  of  selling  a
54:1378:99329:15:15:102:505:393:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pension,  this  will  have  a  significant  impact  on  fund  growth.  This  problem  is
54:1379:99417:15:15:102:505:378:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:exacerbated when employers are small because providers find it more difficult to
54:1380:99497:15:26:102:243:363:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:achieve economies of scale.
54:1381:99524:26:15:90:504:337:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The proposed package of reforms aims to overcome these barriers and enable more
54:1382:99603:15:22:90:166:322:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:people to save.
54:1383:99618:22:15:90:504:300:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The  minimum  employer  contribution  helps  people  to  see  saving  is  valuable,
54:1384:99704:15:15:102:505:285:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:overcoming the informational problems of working out whether to save. The
54:1385:99777:15:15:102:505:270:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:proposed  balance  of  contribution  rates  means  that  the  contribution  by  the
54:1386:99860:15:15:102:505:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individual  is  effectively  matched  by  the  combination  of  the  tax  relief  and  the
54:1387:99950:15:15:102:505:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employer contribution, thus increasing the value of saving. The analysis presented
54:1388:100032:15:15:102:504:225:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in Financial  incentives  to  save  for  retirement40  shows  that  the  employer
54:1389:100113:15:15:102:505:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contribution  and  tax  relief  tends  to  improve  the  incentives  for  individuals  to
54:1390:100202:15:15:102:505:195:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:save. As the incentive to save is increased, the participation rate in pensions also
54:1391:100286:15:15:102:505:180:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increases.  Evidence  shows  that  the  existence  of  an  employer  contribution
54:1392:100367:15:15:102:504:165:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:significantly increases participation in an employer pension41. The existence of
54:1393:100447:15:15:102:505:150:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:an employer contribution is a clear signal to the individual that saving in a pension
54:1394:100532:15:58:102:505:135:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is a good idea, which may overcome some of the behavioural barriers to saving.
54:1395:100610:58:21:90:308:77:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:40McCauley and Sandbrook, forthcoming.
54:1396:100648:21:0:90:173:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:41McKay, 2006.
55:1397:100733:0:89:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
55:1398:100750:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Automatic  enrolment  into  a  pension  will  contribute  towards  overcoming  the
55:1399:100835:15:15:102:505:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:informational problem of working out in which product the individual should
55:1400:100910:15:15:102:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:save. It also tackles behavioural barriers, such as inertia, that currently prevent
55:1401:100993:15:15:102:505:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals from saving, even when they recognise that it is in their interests to
55:1402:101075:15:15:102:505:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:do so. Evidence suggests that automatic enrolment is one of the most effective
55:1403:101153:15:15:102:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:ways of combating people’s tendency not to act when faced with difficult financial
55:1404:101235:15:15:102:505:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:decisions. It will play a key role in achieving high participation rates for personal
55:1405:101320:15:15:102:505:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts and existing employer schemes. The Employers’ Pension Provision 2005
55:1406:101397:15:15:102:505:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:survey findings show a strong link between automatic enrolment and increased
55:1407:101473:15:15:102:505:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:levels  of  pension  scheme  membership.  Within  private  firms  with  20  or  more
55:1408:101557:15:15:102:505:565:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employees,  the  proportion  of  employees  who  were  in  a  pension  averaged
55:1409:101636:15:15:102:505:550:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:60 per cent where the firm used automatic enrolment. This compared to 41 per
55:1410:101712:15:15:102:504:535:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:cent for traditional opt-in pension schemes.42 In case studies of four private sector
55:1411:101797:15:15:102:504:520:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:schemes, automatic enrolment was associated with increased participation rates.43
55:1412:101878:15:15:102:505:505:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:For example, in one firm the participation rate went from 25 per cent for existing
55:1413:101960:15:22:102:489:490:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employees, to 80 per cent for new joiners who were automatically enrolled.
55:1414:102034:22:15:90:504:468:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The design of the personal accounts scheme will tackle the causes of high charges
55:1415:102118:15:15:102:504:453:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in personal pensions, by minimising the reasons for individuals to stop contributing
55:1416:102202:15:15:102:505:438:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to  a  given  pension  fund  and  the  up-front  marketing  and  distribution  costs.
55:1417:102287:15:15:102:505:423:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Through automatic enrolment the need for up-front marketing costs is reduced.
55:1418:102364:15:15:102:505:408:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Furthermore  the  clearing-house  allows  individuals  to  contribute  to  the  same
55:1419:102448:15:15:102:505:393:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:fund  when  they  change  jobs,  which  significantly  reduces  the  cost  and  hence
55:1420:102533:15:15:102:504:378:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:allows a lower annual management charge. This reduction in the charges increases
55:1421:102613:15:15:102:505:363:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  potential  retirement  income  for  an  individual  producing  a  real  efficiency
55:1422:102700:15:26:102:127:348:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:gain.
55:1423:102705:26:15:90:504:322:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:By tackling these inherent problems personal accounts should better enable many
55:1424:102784:15:15:90:504:307:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals  to  save  for  retirement.  Improved  income  and  hence  consumption
55:1425:102866:15:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:smoothing should increase individual welfare. The approach taken in this piece of
55:1426:102947:15:15:90:504:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:work is to focus on the welfare impacts of improved consumption smoothing across
55:1427:103027:15:25:90:153:262:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the lifecycle.
55:1428:103041:25:15:90:504:237:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is possible to look at the benefits of saving in other ways, for example looking just
55:1429:103129:15:15:90:504:222:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:at the financial returns. Financial incentives to save for retirement44 focuses on the
55:1430:103215:15:15:90:504:207:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:financial rewards of saving, but does not account for the relative value of that saving.
55:1431:103303:15:38:90:504:192:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:There  are  also  other  potential  sources  of  welfare  gain  through  the  creation  of
55:1432:103393:38:18:90:505:154:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:42The  difference  in  membership  between  automatic  enrolment  and  traditional
55:1433:103475:18:14:102:505:136:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:opt-in mechanisms is larger when looking at the median level of membership
55:1434:103549:14:17:102:215:122:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rather than the mean.
55:1435:103570:17:18:90:505:105:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:43Horack  and  Wood,  2005.  Note:  other  factors  including  a  required  employee
55:1436:103654:18:14:102:505:87:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contribution, supporting communications and employer commitment may have
55:1437:103726:14:17:102:280:73:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:influenced the outcomes achieved.
55:1438:103759:17:0:90:308:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:44McCauley and Sandbrook, forthcoming.
56:1439:103799:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts; however these are not included in this analysis. One possible
56:1440:103879:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare gain is that individuals saving in personal accounts who would not have
56:1441:103958:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saved  otherwise  may  have  increased  confidence  about  retirement  as  they  have
56:1442:104043:15:37:90:294:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:started to make provision for retirement.
56:1443:104084:37:26:90:224:633:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.3Methodology
56:1444:104098:26:15:90:504:607:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As  explained  in  the  previous  section,  the  approach  taken  to  measure  the  social
56:1445:104188:15:15:90:504:592:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare impact of personal accounts is to consider the value of improved consumption
56:1446:104272:15:15:90:504:577:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:smoothing. Consumption is the economic focus, rather than income smoothing,
56:1447:104347:15:15:90:504:562:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:because it is the actual consumption that is assumed to generate utility not the
56:1448:104427:15:15:90:504:547:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:receipt of income in its own right. However, as consumption is difficult to measure
56:1449:104510:15:15:90:504:532:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:it is assumed that income measures consumption opportunities. Therefore, social
56:1450:104589:15:25:90:420:517:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare changes are measured in this paper by looking at income.
56:1451:104653:25:15:90:504:492:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The methodology employed is relatively simple in outline. It involves estimating the
56:1452:104737:15:15:90:504:477:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:value  of  income  smoothing  for  the  individual  and  aggregating  this  up  to  the
56:1453:104824:15:15:90:504:462:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:population for a given year and then adding together the results over time (we are
56:1454:104906:15:15:90:504:447:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:looking at the period from the introduction of personal accounts in 2012 to 2050).
56:1455:104988:15:15:90:504:432:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The approach taken involves many simplifications and particular assumptions which
56:1456:105069:15:15:90:504:417:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:could have an impact on the results. However, as this paper is an exploration of how
56:1457:105153:15:15:90:504:402:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the welfare impacts could be assessed, using a simplified model allows the most
56:1458:105232:15:25:90:268:387:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:important factors to be considered.
56:1459:105267:25:22:90:187:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Outline of method:
56:1460:105285:22:22:90:404:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:1.    Divide population into groups based on income and age.
56:1461:105345:22:15:90:504:318:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2.    Estimate the weighted NPV of the utility an individual derived from saving in
56:1462:105428:15:23:113:451:303:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts, for representative individuals from each group.
56:1463:105494:23:15:90:504:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:3.    Aggregate NPV of saving to the number of people saving in personal accounts
56:1464:105575:15:15:113:504:265:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in each given year (making an allowance for the proportions of saving that are
56:1465:105653:15:22:113:368:250:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:new and that are transferred from other vehicles).
56:1466:105703:22:15:90:504:228:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:4.    Estimate NPV of the gain over time by in turn discounting NPV for each year
56:1467:105784:15:25:113:376:213:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and aggregating over the time period (2012-2050).
56:1468:105833:25:15:90:504:188:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f7:(1) Segmenting the population: The impact of personal accounts and the default
56:1469:105911:15:15:90:504:173:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contribution level will differ depending on individual characteristics, most importantly
56:1470:105999:15:15:90:504:158:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:age and income level. This is firstly because the income that individuals will receive in
56:1471:106088:15:15:90:504:143:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:retirement from the state will vary over time as the State Pension system evolves.
56:1472:106170:15:15:90:504:128:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Secondly, the income an individual can receive from personal accounts will depend
56:1473:106251:15:15:90:504:113:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:on the length of time they save into personal accounts. To enable these aspects to be
56:1474:106336:15:15:90:504:98:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:captured we have split the population into a number of income groups and age
56:1475:106412:15:0:90:129:83:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:groups.
56:1476:106488:0:89:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
57:1477:106507:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:(2) Estimating the weighted NPV of the utility an individual derived from
57:1478:106580:15:15:90:505:700:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f7:saving  in  personal  accounts:  The  costs  of  pension  saving  occurs  significantly
