57:1479:106667:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:before  the  benefits  are  realised  by  the  individual,  therefore,  we  need  to  use  a
57:1480:106759:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:technique to value costs and benefits that fall in different time periods. The NPV is
57:1481:106844:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:calculated by discounting future benefits and costs using an appropriate rate, and
57:1482:106926:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:subtracting  the  total  of  discounted  costs  from  the  total  of  discounted  benefits.
57:1483:107017:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Discounting takes into account the delay faced by the individual in receiving an
57:1484:107097:15:15:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income stream, in this case the pension. The discount rate can include a variety of
57:1485:107180:15:15:90:504:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:different factors, such as the rate of time preference (which measures the desire to
57:1486:107264:15:15:90:504:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consume now rather than in the future), the uncertainty of the income stream and
57:1487:107344:15:25:90:461:565:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the interest rate that could have been achieved on any investment option.
57:1488:107417:25:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:To estimate the value of the consumption smoothing across the lifecycle we attach
57:1489:107498:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:weights to different levels of consumption. In doing this we have taken a deliberately
57:1490:107584:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:simple approach. Instead of using an inter-temporal consumption function which
57:1491:107662:15:15:90:504:495:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:allows for the optimisation of consumption over time taking into account income,
57:1492:107742:15:15:90:504:480:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the rate of time preference, interest rates and so on, we have adopted a simple
57:1493:107821:15:15:90:504:465:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:approach drawing on the Green Book45. This simplified approach follows the Green
57:1494:107901:15:15:90:504:450:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Book’s approach to measuring the value of redistribution. This approach is based on
57:1495:107984:15:15:90:504:435:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the relative income levels of the individuals whose income is being redistributed. The
57:1496:108070:15:15:90:504:420:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:central assumption is the existence of diminishing marginal utility of consumption,
57:1497:108153:15:15:90:504:405:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which  means  that  an  additional  £1  of  consumption  is  valued  less  as  income
57:1498:108238:15:15:90:504:390:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increases. This assumption implies that individuals with different income levels will
57:1499:108323:15:15:90:504:375:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:have different levels of (marginal) utility. We have adapted this approach to examine
57:1500:108408:15:15:90:504:360:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the impact of redistributing income across the lifetime, in which the welfare impact
57:1501:108492:15:15:90:504:345:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of saving is the value of the redistribution of income between the different time
57:1502:108573:15:25:90:138:330:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:periods46.
57:1503:108583:25:25:90:426:305:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The Green Book adopts a simple functional form to describe utility:
57:1504:108650:25:25:147:281:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Utility = log (consumption)
57:1505:108677:25:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which means that the marginal utility of consumption is equal to the inverse of
57:1506:108756:15:25:90:177:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption, or:
57:1507:108772:25:24:147:218:215:144:g_d0_f11:144:g_d0_f7:δU(c)/δc = 1/c,
57:1508:108787:24:57:90:444:191:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:so if consumption halves, the marginal utility of consumption doubles.
57:1509:108857:57:20:90:204:134:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:45HM Treasury, 2003.
57:1510:108877:20:18:90:505:114:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:46An  underlying  simplifying  assumption  is  that  individuals  have  the  same  utility
57:1511:108967:18:15:102:505:96:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:function throughout their lifetime. We are not exploring redistribution between
57:1512:109046:15:14:102:505:81:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals because this is not a major feature of personal accounts. An alternative
57:1513:109130:14:14:102:505:67:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:would  be  to  use  an  intertemporal  utility  function,  however,  the  Green  Book
57:1514:109215:14:0:102:454:53:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:framework adopted here would not be feasible under this approach.
57:1515:109349:0:89:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
58:1516:109368:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Thus to take a pension example, an individual, who earns £20,000 while working,
58:1517:109447:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:receives £10,000 in State Pensions. He/she contributes £1,000 to a private pension
58:1518:109529:15:25:90:285:685:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:which pays out £1,000 in retirement.47
58:1519:109567:25:25:147:458:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:utility gained = pension/retirement income = £1,000/£10,000
58:1520:109626:25:25:147:481:635:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:utility foregone = contribution/working income = £1,000/£20,000
58:1521:109689:25:25:90:357:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Net change in utility = utility gained – utility foregone
58:1522:109746:25:25:147:238:585:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:= 1,000/20,000 48
58:1523:109763:25:15:90:504:560:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Multiplying  this  abstract  gain  of  1,000/20,000  units  of  utility  with  working  life
58:1524:109855:15:24:90:301:545:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income, we arrive at a net gain of £1,000.
58:1525:109897:24:15:90:504:521:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Although  individuals  seek  to  smooth  their  income  into  retirement,  evidence
58:1526:109980:15:15:90:504:506:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:suggests that unconstrained individuals do not seek to fully replace their in-work
58:1527:110062:15:15:90:504:491:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income, and that gross replacement rates, the ratio of retirement income to in-work
58:1528:110145:15:15:90:504:476:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income, of less than 100 per cent will deliver the same living standards in retirement
58:1529:110231:15:15:90:504:461:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:as they do in working life. This is due to the fact that individuals often face lower
58:1530:110316:15:15:90:504:446:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:expenditure in retirement, for example, because they no longer face work related
58:1531:110396:15:15:90:504:431:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:costs, they may have paid off their mortgage, they no longer have to pay pension or
58:1532:110479:15:15:90:504:416:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:national  insurance  contributions,  or  indeed  because  some  of  the  consumption
58:1533:110563:15:15:90:504:401:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:during their working lives is now compensated for by more State Pension age time.
58:1534:110644:15:15:90:504:386:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:We  have,  therefore,  adapted  the  weighting  approach  to  take  into  account  the
58:1535:110730:15:15:90:504:371:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:benchmark  replacement  rates  used  by  the  Pensions  Commission,  which  was
58:1536:110809:15:15:90:504:356:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:confirmed through a later survey which asked individuals about their desired income
58:1537:110892:15:15:90:504:341:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in retirement.49 Figure 4.1 shows the range of replacement rates used, which vary
58:1538:110973:15:15:90:504:326:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:according to income as it is assumed that individuals with higher earnings do not
58:1539:111054:15:200:90:501:311:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:need to replace as much income in retirement to maintain their standard of living.
58:1540:111136:200:18:90:505:111:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:47This example is simplified, so the impact of tax relief and investment growth is
58:1541:111218:18:16:102:169:93:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:not included.
58:1542:111231:16:21:90:315:77:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:48The unit ‘£’ cancels out in the calculation.
58:1543:111277:21:0:90:249:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:49Pensions Commission, 2005.
58:1544:111374:0:88:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
59:1545:111393:88:14:90:488:716:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Figure 4.1Benchmark replacement rates assumed for pensions
59:1546:111451:14:280:175:491:702:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:commission modelling: percentage of gross earnings
59:1547:111501:280:15:90:504:422:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Saving in personal accounts at the default level will not necessarily put individuals on
59:1548:111589:15:15:90:504:407:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their benchmark replacement rate; however, it will enable more individuals to move
59:1549:111671:15:15:90:504:392:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:closer to their target level of provision. The benchmark replacement rate for the
59:1550:111752:15:15:90:504:377:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:median earner according to the Pensions Commission is 67 per cent. To adapt the
59:1551:111831:15:15:90:504:362:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:marginal utility of consumption equation to account for individuals not wanting 100
59:1552:111914:15:15:90:504:347:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:per cent replacement rate we create a weighting function based on how close the
59:1553:111993:15:15:90:504:332:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individual is to the benchmark replacement rate. The closer someone gets to the
59:1554:112072:15:15:90:504:317:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:benchmark  replacement  rate  the  smaller  the  weighting.  The  replacement  rate
59:1555:112155:15:15:90:504:302:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:measures income, but this is assumed to act as a proxy for levels of consumption
59:1556:112235:15:15:90:504:287:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:both in work and in retirement as consumption opportunities are based on income
59:1557:112314:15:15:90:504:272:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:over  an  individual’s  lifetime.  The  weighting  function,  W,  is  estimated  using  the
59:1558:112405:15:25:90:194:257:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:following equations:
59:1559:112425:25:15:90:435:232:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:W=  Benchmark consumption *(1/consumption in retirement)
59:1560:112481:15:15:133:464:217:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:=  Benchmark replacement rate * (1/achieved replacement rate in
59:1561:112544:15:15:147:203:202:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:retirement)
59:1562:112555:15:15:133:293:187:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:=Benchmark replacement rate
59:1563:112582:15:25:147:282:172:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Achieved replacement rate
59:1564:112607:25:15:90:504:147:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Therefore, if an individual were seeking to fully replace their income, the value of
59:1565:112691:15:15:90:504:132:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:redistributing  income  from  working  life  to  retirement  would  be  identical  to  the
59:1566:112781:15:15:90:504:117:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:original unweighted formula above. However, if the benchmark replacement rate is
59:1567:112861:15:15:90:504:102:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:less than full replacement of income, then the weight applied to the consumption
59:1568:112941:15:25:90:227:87:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:function will adjust for this.
59:1569:112971:25:15:90:504:62:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Table 4.1 sets out the range of weightings used for this analysis based on someone
59:1570:113053:15:15:90:504:47:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with earnings just above the median. The high weighting is based on the replacement
59:1571:113136:15:0:90:504:32:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rate  achieved  from  state  provision  alone.  The  first  pound  of  saving,  therefore,
59:1572:113295:0:89:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
60:1573:113314:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increases  people’s  replacement  rate  from  this  point  and,  therefore,  is  the  most
60:1574:113404:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:valuable  slice  of  redistribution  given  our  assumed  shape  of  the  consumption
60:1575:113489:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:function. The low weighting is based on the replacement rate the median earner
60:1576:113567:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:would achieve if they saved in personal accounts at the minimum level throughout
60:1577:113647:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working life.50 This approach measures the value of the final £1 put into personal
60:1578:113729:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts, which is the least valuable slice of redistribution. The central assumption is
60:1579:113817:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the average of these two and can be seen as the weighting on the average pound
60:1580:113895:15:33:90:260:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contributed to personal accounts.
60:1581:113928:33:14:90:495:577:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Table 4.1Weighting factors applied under the different scenarios
60:1582:113992:14:29:161:384:563:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:assuming annual earnings of £25,000
60:1583:114027:29:15:90:469:534:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Benchmark replacement rate60%
60:1584:114056:15:15:90:469:519:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Replacement rate achieved with no saving34%
60:1585:114099:15:15:90:469:504:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Replacement rate achieved with saving at default level45%
60:1586:114156:15:15:90:466:489:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:High weighting (benchmark replacement rate/replacement rate with no saving)1.8
60:1587:114234:15:15:90:466:474:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Low weighting (benchmark replacement rate/replacement rate with saving)1.3
60:1588:114308:15:32:90:466:459:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Average weighting1.6
60:1589:114328:32:15:90:504:427:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The achieved replacement rate is based on the State Pension system proposed in the
60:1590:114410:15:15:90:504:412:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:White  Paper  and  has  been  measured  on  a  gross  income  basis,  but  including
60:1591:114494:15:25:90:249:397:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:entitlement to Pension Credit.51
60:1592:114526:25:15:90:504:372:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The next step in estimating the weighted NPV of pension saving is to estimate the
60:1593:114607:15:15:90:504:357:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income stream produced by pension saving. This is estimated by calculating the
60:1594:114685:15:15:90:504:342:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:pension pot that an individual can accumulate over time from saving £1 in personal
60:1595:114767:15:15:90:504:327:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts.  When  the  person  reaches  State  Pension  age,  it  is  assumed  that  they
60:1596:114855:15:15:90:504:312:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:annuitise this income which then produces a guaranteed income for each year of
60:1597:114933:15:15:90:504:297:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their  retirement.  Then,  to  estimate  the  weighted  NPV  the  annuity  income  is
60:1598:115018:15:15:90:504:282:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:weighted by the appropriate factor and then discounted to account for the delay in
60:1599:115100:15:25:90:244:267:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:receiving this income stream52.
60:1600:115131:25:15:90:504:242:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Not all saving in personal accounts is assumed to be new saving. It is likely that some
60:1601:115218:15:15:90:504:227:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of the saving in personal accounts is saving transferred from other vehicles. We
60:1602:115298:15:29:90:504:212:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimate  that  there  is  a  positive  value  to  this  transfer  of  saving,  because  if  an
60:1603:115393:29:18:90:505:183:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:50In this model we have simplified the contribution rate to be eight per cent for
60:1604:115474:18:15:102:505:165:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  individual,  which  takes  into  account  the  individual’s  and  the  employer’s
60:1605:115560:15:14:102:505:150:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:contributions as well as tax relief. Our model does not consider possible second-
60:1606:115641:14:14:102:505:136:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:round  effects  of  employer  contributions,  such  as  employers  passing  on  extra
60:1607:115726:14:15:102:505:122:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:costs through wages or prices, which would change the impact on the gains to
60:1608:115802:15:14:102:505:107:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals, as these are extremely difficult to predict. This does not, however,
60:1609:115883:14:15:102:505:93:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:make our model less robust, as it is still able to give a useful indication of the
60:1610:115965:15:16:102:428:78:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:social welfare benefits of the introduction of personal accounts.
60:1611:116030:16:20:90:481:62:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:51Entitlement to Council Tax Benefit has been excluded from this modelling.
60:1612:116105:20:0:90:438:42:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:52Assuming the whole fund is converted to an index linked annuity.
60:1613:116240:0:89:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
61:1614:116259:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individual, switches personal accounts are likely to have lower charges than the
61:1615:116339:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:other  vehicles.  To  estimate  the  value  of  switching  saving  the  weighted  NPV  is
61:1616:116428:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:calculated for the original savings vehicle (assumed to have stakeholder pension
61:1617:116508:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:charges of 1.5 per cent AMC for the first ten years with one per cent AMC thereafter)
61:1618:116593:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and the gain from switching is the difference between the weighted NPV for other
61:1619:116673:15:25:90:390:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saving compared to the NPV of saving in personal accounts.
61:1620:116731:25:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Table 4.2 sets out the estimated NPV and weighted NPV for a man aged 30 in 2012
61:1621:116810:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:making a £1 contribution to personal accounts in 2012 using the low weighting
61:1622:116887:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:factor. This shows that if the income for personal accounts is not weighted there is
61:1623:116971:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:no welfare gain for saving in a personal account; this is because we conservatively
61:1624:117054:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assume that the discount rate applied to future income is greater than the net return
61:1625:117139:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:achieved on saving. However, once the value of redistribution of income over time is
61:1626:117223:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:included there is a gain from saving in a pension. It can be beneficial for individuals
61:1627:117310:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:who are currently saving into other savings products with similar expected returns to
61:1628:117395:15:15:90:504:495:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:cease to do so and start saving in personal accounts provided that charges on the
61:1629:117476:15:33:90:245:480:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:former are comparatively high.
61:1630:117506:33:14:90:468:447:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Table 4.2Net present value of saving £1 for a man aged 30 in
61:1631:117566:14:29:161:278:433:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:2012 saving in 2012
61:1632:117585:29:12:361:482:404:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:Net presentWeighted
61:1633:117604:12:20:375:468:392:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:valueNPV
61:1634:117612:20:14:90:471:372:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:In personal accounts-£0.13£0.20
61:1635:117643:14:20:90:471:358:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:In personal accounts instead of other savings product£0.17£0.23
61:1636:117706:20:12:90:473:338:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Notes: The NPV of saving in personal accounts is negative because the simplified approach
61:1637:117795:12:12:90:493:326:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:assumes that all contributions (eight per cent) are made by individuals. If this was calculated on
61:1638:117893:12:12:90:496:314:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:the share of contributions actually made by individuals (four per cent) this would be significantly
61:1639:117992:12:28:90:119:302:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:higher.
61:1640:117999:28:15:90:504:274:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f7:(3) Aggregating the results to the population: We are assuming a simple, non-
61:1641:118076:15:15:90:504:259:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:weighted, utilitarian, aggregate welfare function as the sum of individual utilities.
61:1642:118161:15:15:90:504:244:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Therefore, to estimate the social welfare gain we have to aggregate the individual
61:1643:118243:15:15:90:504:229:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:utility functions. Thus the approach is to aggregate the estimated weighted NPV for
61:1644:118326:15:15:90:504:214:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:each sub group weighted by the relative size of the group. This is based on estimates
61:1645:118411:15:25:90:440:199:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:by the DWP of the group likely to be in personal accounts over time.53
61:1646:118481:25:15:90:504:174:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The benefit of saving is estimated by calculating the value of each £1 contribution.
61:1647:118565:15:15:90:504:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Therefore, to be able to add each group together, we estimate the total contribution
61:1648:118649:15:15:90:504:144:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:made each year by each group, which is eight per cent of earnings between £5,000
61:1649:118729:15:15:90:504:129:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and £33,000. Then, to estimate the total welfare gain of personal accounts, this is
61:1650:118812:15:58:90:471:114:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:multiplied by the weighted NPV of that group for that year of contributions.
61:1651:118888:58:0:90:164:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:53DWP, 2006.
61:1652:118969:0:89:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
62:1653:118988:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As we have explained above, a proportion of saving in personal accounts will be
62:1654:119067:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saving  diverted  from  other  forms  of  saving.  A  research  report,  conducted  by
62:1655:119153:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:PricewaterhouseCoopers, examining the likely impact on savings levels of personal
62:1656:119234:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts,  supports  an  assumption  that  a  significant  part  of  saving  in  personal
62:1657:119323:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts  will  be  new  saving.54  Therefore,  in  aggregating  the  results  we  have
62:1658:119410:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assumed that a proportion (60 per cent) of the contributions made by each sub-
62:1659:119488:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:group each year is new saving, and has the weighted NPV of personal accounts
62:1660:119564:15:15:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:applied  to  the  contributions.  The  rest  of  the  saving  is  switched  saving,  so  that
62:1661:119657:15:15:90:504:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:proportion  of  contributions  (40  per  cent)  is  multiplied  by  the  weighted  NPV  of
62:1662:119747:15:25:90:173:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:switched saving.
62:1663:119763:25:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f7:(4) Estimating the NPV over time: Once the aggregate NPV of contributions in
62:1664:119839:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:each year has been calculated, as set out above, this can be used to estimate the
62:1665:119920:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:social  welfare  impact  over  time.  This  is  estimated  by  taking  the  estimate  of  the
62:1666:120013:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:benefit of contributions in each year and calculating the net present value of this
62:1667:120096:15:15:90:504:495:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:series. This has to be a discounted sum of the individual years’ benefits, because the
62:1668:120182:15:15:90:504:480:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in-year estimate is estimating the value of the contributions in that year, and then we
62:1669:120269:15:15:90:504:465:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:need to discount that back to today to estimate the value of the increase in wellbeing
62:1670:120355:15:37:90:407:450:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:resulting from the introduction of personal accounts over time.
62:1671:120418:37:26:90:429:413:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.4Limitations and weaknesses in methodology
62:1672:120462:26:15:90:504:387:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This approach and method to estimate the welfare gain from personal accounts is
62:1673:120541:15:15:90:504:372:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:simplified as it is an exploration of how the welfare impacts of personal accounts
62:1674:120623:15:15:90:504:357:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:could be estimated. There are a number of things that have been excluded from the
62:1675:120704:15:25:90:304:342:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:analysis which could impact on the results.
62:1676:120747:25:15:90:504:317:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The model is only including the impact of contributions made between 2012 and
62:1677:120824:15:15:90:504:302:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2050. It is likely that the impact of personal accounts on savings behaviour will
62:1678:120905:15:15:90:504:287:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:continue past this point, therefore, the welfare impact will continue over time, and
62:1679:120989:15:25:90:228:272:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:potentially increase further.
62:1680:121018:25:15:90:504:247:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The analysis of what income individuals receive in retirement is based on constant
62:1681:121100:15:15:90:504:232:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earnings profiles and there is no account taken of household size neither during
62:1682:121180:15:25:90:333:217:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals’ working lives nor in their retirement.
62:1683:121231:25:15:90:504:192:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This means that in retirement individuals’ welfare position is based only on their own
62:1684:121317:15:15:90:504:177:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:earnings  and  contributions  history,  not  on  the  position  of  their  household.  The
62:1685:121407:15:15:90:504:162:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:simplified consumption function does not account for whether individuals would
62:1686:121485:15:15:90:504:147:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:choose to save in a different pattern depending on their household size (such as
62:1687:121565:15:15:90:504:132:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saving very little when they have young children and then saving more when the
62:1688:121643:15:61:90:198:117:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:children leave home).
62:1689:121664:61:0:90:204:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:54Hawksworth, 2006.
62:1690:121752:0:89:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
63:1691:121771:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:However, in using an individual basis to consider savings decisions we are following
63:1692:121855:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the treatment by Kirsavnova and Sefton, (2006), which was informed by empirical
63:1693:121934:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:work showing that lifecycle savings patterns could be identified at the individual but
63:1694:122020:15:25:90:200:670:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:not household level.55
63:1695:122042:25:15:90:504:645:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As mentioned above, our analysis uses a simple earnings function in which each
63:1696:122120:15:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individual has constant earnings in earnings terms throughout their working life.
63:1697:122201:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The value of saving is measured relative to a replacement rate target and an estimate
63:1698:122286:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of  State  Pension  entitlement  which  assumes  constant  earnings  over  time.  If
63:1699:122370:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals benefit from earnings which vary in earnings terms over time, the value of
63:1700:122456:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:redistribution over their lifetime will have a different pattern. However, if individuals
63:1701:122545:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:retirement aspirations are based on their income towards the end of their working
63:1702:122626:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:life, the value of redistributing income from working life to retirement is likely to be
63:1703:122714:15:15:90:504:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:higher, which means the welfare gain could be larger. To fully account for this the
63:1704:122797:15:15:90:504:510:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:model would have to allow individuals to defer saving to later in working life when
63:1705:122880:15:15:90:504:495:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:their income is higher once discount rates and investment returns are taken into
63:1706:122960:15:25:90:412:480:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:account, which was beyond the scope of this exploratory paper.
63:1707:123022:25:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The log utility function as adopted by the Green Book has been chosen to be in line
63:1708:123105:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:with Government best practice in evaluating policy options, but is also supported by
63:1709:123189:15:15:90:504:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a wide range of academic research and avoids having to make more assumptions
63:1710:123265:15:15:90:504:410:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:about parameters than is strictly necessary. This is a simplification, but it is precisely
63:1711:123355:15:15:90:504:395:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:for this reason that log utility is agreed in academic circles to be extremely useful for
63:1712:123444:15:15:90:504:380:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:modelling purposes.56 One assumption within the log utility function is that there is
63:1713:123529:15:15:90:504:365:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:no accounting for risk aversion. This means that the variation in investment returns
63:1714:123613:15:15:90:504:350:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and the impact this could have on individuals, in affecting their final income, but also
63:1715:123701:15:15:90:504:335:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in  creating  uncertainty  about  retirement  income  during  working  life  has  been
63:1716:123787:15:15:90:504:320:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:excluded. If the variation in investment returns was considerable, then this could
63:1717:123869:15:15:90:504:305:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:reduce any aggregate welfare benefit. However, if higher estimates of risk aversion
63:1718:123952:15:15:90:504:290:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:were included, this would increase the value of redistributing income to retirement
63:1719:124035:15:25:90:275:275:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:to avoid large drops in consumption.
63:1720:124071:25:15:90:504:250:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In addition to these limitations of the adopted model, potential second best effects
63:1721:124155:15:15:90:504:235:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:on other related potentially distorted markets have not been quantified but we do
63:1722:124236:15:15:90:504:220:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:not expect them to be large. We have identified two markets which may both be
63:1723:124313:15:15:90:504:205:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:distorted  and  be  affected  by  the  introduction  of  personal  accounts:  the  labour
63:1724:124402:15:113:90:388:190:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:market for older workers and the market for personal debt.
63:1725:124460:113:21:90:253:77:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:55Kirsavnova and Sefton, 2006.
63:1726:124490:21:0:90:264:56:49:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:56See, for example, Romer, 2001.
63:1727:124591:0:89:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
64:1728:124610:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  An alternative to saving more for retirement is to work for longer, and, as the
64:1729:124692:15:15:102:505:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:White Paper identifies, the labour market for older workers is currently distorted
64:1730:124774:15:15:102:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and  older  workers  may  find  it  difficult  to  find  jobs  which  are  flexible  to  their
64:1731:124868:15:15:102:505:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:requirements. Therefore, the introduction of personal accounts, which will enable
64:1732:124949:15:15:102:505:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:more people to save more for retirement, may mean that the distortions of the
64:1733:125026:15:15:102:505:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:labour market become less significant to individuals, which will improve welfare.
64:1734:125107:15:15:102:505:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:However, the magnitude of this benefit is not possible to measure and would in
64:1735:125185:15:15:102:505:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:any event be reduced by policies on extending working life in the White Paper
64:1736:125262:15:15:102:505:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:since they should improve the efficiency of the labour market. Chapter 2 sets
64:1737:125339:15:15:102:505:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:out the impacts of longer working lives on GDP and Chapter 3 sets out combined
64:1738:125417:15:15:102:504:565:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:macroeconomic modelling of both changes in saving as well as changes in working
64:1739:125496:15:22:102:121:550:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:life.
64:1740:125501:22:15:90:504:528:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Individuals  can  choose  between  saving  and  repaying  borrowing  to  smooth
64:1741:125583:15:15:102:505:513:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption,  and  there  are  worries  that  the  market  for  short-term  debt  is
64:1742:125667:15:15:102:505:498:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:distorted by excessive marketing and some of the same behavioural economics
64:1743:125742:15:15:102:505:483:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:issues that impact on long-term saving. The introduction of automatic enrolment
64:1744:125821:15:15:102:505:468:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is  intended  to  lead  to  more  individuals  saving  for  retirement,  but  it  may  also
64:1745:125912:15:15:102:505:453:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:encourage  some  individuals  to  take  out  short-term  loans  to  finance  current
64:1746:125996:15:15:102:505:438:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption. This may then lead to a further distortion to individuals’ portfolios
64:1747:126078:15:15:102:505:423:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:as they find themselves with significant short-term debt and inaccessible long-
64:1748:126157:15:15:102:505:408:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:term savings with a lower rate of return, which reduces the welfare gains from
64:1749:126235:15:15:102:505:393:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts. We believe that many people with expensive debts will opt
64:1750:126311:15:15:102:505:378:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:out of personal accounts (partly as a result of information products specifically
64:1751:126392:15:26:102:381:363:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:targeted at this group), and that the cost will be small.
64:1752:126449:26:15:90:504:337:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This  analysis  of  the  income  smoothing  impacts  of  personal  accounts  does  not
64:1753:126535:15:15:90:504:322:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:include anything on the potential welfare effects of increased savings leading to
64:1754:126616:15:15:90:504:307:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:higher economic growth, or the economic impact of reduced consumption during
64:1755:126692:15:15:90:504:292:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working  life.  Chapter  3  explores  the  macroeconomic  impacts  of  the  reform
64:1756:126774:15:15:90:504:277:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:package. This paper does not attempt to measure other aspects of increased welfare
64:1757:126856:15:15:90:504:262:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:from saving, such as the increased sense of security about retirement as a result of
64:1758:126940:15:37:90:125:247:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saving.
64:1759:126947:37:25:90:220:210:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.5Assumptions
64:1760:126961:25:23:90:193:185:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Our model assumes:
64:1761:126979:23:15:90:504:162:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  3.5 per cent real rate of return, which is reduced by 0.5 per cent for saving in
64:1762:127062:15:15:102:505:147:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal  accounts  or  by  1.5  per  cent  for  the  first  ten  years  and  one  per  cent
64:1763:127154:15:0:102:494:132:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:thereafter in other pensions, to account for the annual management charge.
64:1764:127297:0:89:435:536:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
65:1765:127316:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  A social discount rate of 3.5 per cent in the short-term (then decreased to long-
65:1766:127400:15:15:102:505:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:term rate of three per cent to account for uncertainty) as recommended in the
65:1767:127477:15:15:102:505:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Green Book guidance. The rate of return does not exceed the discount rate in
65:1768:127553:15:15:102:505:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:our model, which thus avoids illusory welfare gains. If looked at on an individual
65:1769:127635:15:15:102:505:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:level  discount  rates  may  of  course  vary,  but  in  the  context  of  this  model  it  is
65:1770:127729:15:15:102:505:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:neither practical nor useful to apply a variety of different rates. Instead we apply
65:1771:127813:15:15:102:505:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a  sensible  social  discount  rate  in  line  with  based  on  the  Green  Book
65:1772:127893:15:22:102:205:610:144:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:recommendations;57
65:1773:127911:22:15:90:504:588:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  An annuity rate of 5.6 per cent based on a single-life price linked annuity with
65:1774:127994:15:23:102:362:573:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:20 year life expectancy is purchased with the fund;
65:1775:128045:23:22:90:340:550:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  Personal accounts are introduced in 2012; and
65:1776:128093:22:38:90:504:528:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:•  The net present value is calculated on the benefits of contributions up to 2050.
65:1777:128176:38:26:90:180:490:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.6Results

65:1797:129173:0:93:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
66:1798:129192:93:25:90:210:711:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.7Sensitivities
66:1799:129208:25:15:90:504:686:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:As this analysis is driven by assumptions, it is important to look at the impact of
66:1800:129291:15:15:90:504:671:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:varying  assumptions.  We  look  in  turn  at  the  key  sensitivities,  while  using  our
66:1801:129381:15:15:90:504:656:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:estimates on the additionality of saving (central at 60 per cent) and the weighting of
66:1802:129467:15:15:90:504:641:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income at their respective central levels and keeping the assumptions on stakeholder
66:1803:129551:15:15:90:504:626:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:annual  management  charges,  annuity  rates  and  life  expectancy  post  retirement
66:1804:129636:15:25:90:137:611:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:constant.
66:1805:129645:25:15:90:504:586:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:It is likely that the discount rate and the rate of return over time move in line, if there
66:1806:129736:15:15:90:504:571:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:is a significant difference between the discount rate and the rate of return then the
66:1807:129821:15:15:90:504:556:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:rate of return will change over time in response to the level of available capital. Table
66:1808:129910:15:15:90:504:541:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:2.3 sets out the impact of the discount rate and rate of return jointly varying while
66:1809:129995:15:15:90:504:526:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:holding the other assumptions constant. Reducing the discount rate and rate of
66:1810:130073:15:15:90:504:511:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:return increases the social welfare gain, because the impact of the discount rate
66:1811:130154:15:15:90:504:496:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:dominates. The lower discount rate significantly increases the benefits as individuals
66:1812:130240:15:33:90:324:481:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:become more willing to wait for consumption.
66:1813:130284:33:14:90:499:448:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Table 4.4Sensitivity analysis of varying the discount rate and rate
66:1814:130351:14:30:161:215:434:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:of return
66:1815:130360:30:15:280:455:404:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:Discount rate and gross rate of return
66:1816:130398:15:12:265:471:389:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:2.5%Central assumption4.5%
66:1817:130424:12:19:264:472:377:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:£ (bn)£ (bn)£ (bn)
66:1818:130442:19:33:90:464:358:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Welfare benefit554535
66:1819:130463:33:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:By varying replacement rates we change the weighting applied, which measure the
66:1820:130542:15:15:90:504:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:value  of  redistribution.  In  the  high  case,  benchmark  replacement  rates  are  ten
66:1821:130631:15:15:90:504:295:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:percentage points higher than they were in the central case. This has the impact of
66:1822:130714:15:15:90:504:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increasing the high weighting for the median earner, presented in Table 2.2 from
66:1823:130794:15:15:90:504:265:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:1.6  to  1.9.  However,  the  impact  of  increase  in  replacement  rates  is  dampened
66:1824:130882:15:15:90:504:250:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:because although the weighted NPV of saving in personal accounts increases, the
66:1825:130961:15:15:90:504:235:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:weighted NPV of switching saving from other vehicles remains constant. This is
66:1826:131039:15:15:90:504:220:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:because  the  value  of  switching  is  the  difference  between  the  weighted  NPV  of
66:1827:131127:15:15:90:504:205:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:saving in a Personal Account and other vehicles, and these move together when the
66:1828:131208:15:32:90:273:190:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:target replacement rate is increased.
66:1829:131245:32:14:90:496:158:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:Table 4.5Sensitivity analysis of different benchmark replacement
66:1830:131309:14:30:161:191:144:169:g_d0_f6:169:g_d0_f6:rates

67:1836:131504:89:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The impact of changing the annual management charge to 0.4 per cent or to 0.6 per
67:1837:131585:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:cent also impacts on the welfare gain, as this affects the efficiency gain from saving
67:1838:131671:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in  personal  accounts  relative  to  stakeholders  as  well  as  affecting  the  gain  from

67:1840:131852:15:33:90:129:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:smaller.

67:1845:131988:12:19:264:472:552:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f6:£ (bn)£ (bn)£ (bn)
67:1846:132006:19:46:90:464:533:100:g_d0_f7:100:g_d0_f7:Welfare benefit504540
67:1847:132027:46:25:90:209:487:256:g_d0_f7:256:g_d0_f7:4.8Conclusion
67:1848:132040:25:15:90:504:462:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This  analysis  suggests  that  a  conservative  estimate  of  the  social  welfare  gain
67:1849:132129:15:15:90:504:447:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:associated with the introduction of personal accounts enabling better consumption
67:1850:132210:15:15:90:504:432:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:smoothing across the lifecycle is substantial and positive. This estimate is subject to
67:1851:132297:15:15:90:504:417:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:a wide range of uncertainty. However, this method of estimating a welfare gain
67:1852:132375:15:15:90:504:402:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:from increased saving and quantification does suggest that there is a benefit to
67:1853:132455:15:0:90:283:387:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:society in increasing savings over time.
67:1854:132564:0:241:59:160:804:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:personal accounts
68:1855:132583:241:40:90:284:563:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:5   Conclusion
68:1856:132597:40:15:90:504:523:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f9:The  Government  White  Paper  Security  in  retirement:  towards  a  new  pensions
68:1857:132680:15:15:90:504:508:144:g_d0_f9:144:g_d0_f7:system,  published  in  May  2006,  contained  a  pension  reform  package  that  is
68:1858:132764:15:15:90:504:493:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:designed to provide a long-lasting framework. It also announced the intention to
68:1859:132844:15:15:90:504:478:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:produce  this  technical  paper,  to  assess  in  more  detail  the  economic  and  social
68:1860:132934:15:15:90:504:463:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare  impacts  of  two  particular  aspects  of  the  reforms,  the  introduction  of
68:1861:133022:15:15:90:504:448:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal  accounts  and  measures  to  extend  working  life.  This  paper  explored
68:1862:133106:15:15:90:504:433:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:possible  methodological  approaches  to  measuring  economic  and  social  welfare
68:1863:133189:15:15:90:504:418:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects and provided quantitative estimates. This paper is not a definitive statement
68:1864:133274:15:15:90:504:403:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:on the magnitude of the effects of pension reform, about which there is substantial
68:1865:133357:15:25:90:455:388:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:uncertainty, but suggests the direction and possible scale of the impacts.
68:1866:133431:25:15:90:504:363:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:This  paper  has  looked  at  two  different  ways  of  measuring  the  impact  of  the
68:1867:133518:15:15:90:504:348:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:introduction of State Pension age policies and personal accounts. It first considered
68:1868:133603:15:15:90:504:333:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic effects, in the context of which two complementary approaches are used.
68:1869:133683:15:15:90:504:318:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The first is a partial approach that can quickly provide estimates of the economic
68:1870:133765:15:15:90:504:303:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects of increasing State Pension age based on assumptions around changes in
68:1871:133843:15:15:90:504:288:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:employment  rates.  The  second,  more  comprehensive,  method  uses  NiGEM,  a
68:1872:133922:15:15:90:504:273:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:macroeconomic model of the UK economy developed by the National Institute of
68:1873:133998:15:15:90:504:258:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Economic and Social Research (NIESR). With this model, both the economic effects
68:1874:134078:15:15:90:504:243:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of increases in State Pension age and the introduction of personal accounts were
68:1875:134158:15:15:90:504:228:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:analysed. Finally, an innovative method to estimate the social welfare impacts of
68:1876:134239:15:24:90:263:213:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts was developed.
68:1877:134271:24:15:90:504:189:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:In measuring the economic impacts, two measures of the size of the economy were
68:1878:134350:15:15:90:504:174:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:used. Firstly, gross domestic product (GDP), which is a measure of the total value of
68:1879:134435:15:15:90:504:159:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:final goods and services produced within a country’s borders in a year. Secondly,
68:1880:134516:15:15:90:504:144:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:gross national product (GNP) which is the value of all goods and services produced
68:1881:134598:15:15:90:504:129:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:in a country in one year, plus income earned by its residents abroad, minus income
68:1882:134680:15:25:90:218:114:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:payable to non-residents.
68:1883:134705:25:15:90:504:89:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Chapter  2  used  a  simple  microeconomic  approach  to  estimate  the  impact  of
68:1884:134788:15:15:90:504:74:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:increasing  State  Pension  age.  The  analysis  suggests  that  the  changes  to  State
68:1885:134876:15:15:90:504:59:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Pension age and the associated polices to extend working lives will have a positive
68:1886:134959:15:0:90:504:44:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic impact through additional labour supplied by older workers. In the central
69:1887:135054:0:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:scenario, this would increase GDP by around 1.4 per cent. The chapter presents a
69:1888:135134:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:range of results to reflect the uncertainty surrounding the employment response. In
69:1889:135217:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the  analysis,  the  uncertainty  surrounding  future  trends  in  the  earnings  of  older
69:1890:135308:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:workers is also discussed and sensitivity analysis shows to what extent different
69:1891:135389:15:25:90:413:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assumptions on earnings profiles would lead to different results.
69:1892:135454:25:15:90:504:630:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The subsequent chapter used a dynamic general equilibrium model to assess the
69:1893:135531:15:15:90:504:615:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:macroeconomic impact of increasing State Pension age as well as the introduction
69:1894:135611:15:15:90:504:600:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of  personal  accounts.  The  results  show  that  the  impact  of  personal  accounts  is
69:1895:135701:15:15:90:504:585:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:mainly on incomes (as reflected in GNP) and is small but positive. In our central
69:1896:135782:15:15:90:504:570:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:scenario, incomes are 0.2 per cent higher in the long term. The impact of longer
69:1897:135862:15:15:90:504:555:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:working is both on GDP and incomes and is estimated to be substantially larger. In
69:1898:135944:15:15:90:504:540:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:our central scenario, GDP increases by 1.7 per cent, with incomes being 2.0 per cent
69:1899:136028:15:25:90:126:525:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:higher.
69:1900:136035:25:15:90:504:500:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Both sets of simulations were subjected to alternative scenarios and sensitivities. The
69:1901:136122:15:15:90:504:485:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:alternative scenarios show a relatively wide range of possible impacts, but they all
69:1902:136206:15:15:90:504:470:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:remain  clearly  positive.  Our  sensitivity  analysis  has  mainly  focussed  on  when
69:1903:136293:15:15:90:504:455:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economic agents (i.e. consumers, businesses) incorporate knowledge of the new
69:1904:136370:15:15:90:504:440:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:policies into their behaviour. If economic agents act as if they have absolutely no
69:1905:136453:15:15:90:504:425:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:prior knowledge, the short-term effects tend to be amplified, though long-term
69:1906:136531:15:15:90:504:410:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:effects tend to be roughly the same as in the case when economic agents anticipate
69:1907:136613:15:25:90:175:395:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the new policies.
69:1908:136630:25:15:90:504:370:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The final section showed what would happen if the effects of the two sets of policies
69:1909:136715:15:15:90:504:355:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:were additive. It was argued that in practice this would not be wholly the case, as
69:1910:136798:15:15:90:504:340:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal accounts would likely be an important vehicle for the additional savings
69:1911:136879:15:15:90:504:325:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that would result from individuals adjusting their life expectancy by three years. The
69:1912:136965:15:15:90:504:310:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:overall impact of changes to State Pension age and the introduction of personal
69:1913:137044:15:15:90:504:295:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:accounts on UK incomes is likely to be in the range of 0.9-3.1 per cent. In terms of
69:1914:137128:15:25:90:395:280:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:today’s economy, this is equivalent to around £11-38 billion.
69:1915:137189:25:15:90:504:255:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The  fourth  and  final  chapter  developed  a  methodology  to  estimate  the  social
69:1916:137275:15:15:90:504:240:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare benefit of introducing personal accounts by aggregating the welfare of all
69:1917:137357:15:15:90:504:225:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:individuals in society. The results suggest that a conservative estimate of the social
69:1918:137443:15:15:90:504:210:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:welfare gain associated with the introduction of personal accounts - which enables
69:1919:137525:15:25:90:484:195:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:better consumption smoothing across the lifecycle - is substantial and positive.
69:1920:137605:25:15:90:504:170:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The estimates of the different impact presented in this paper should not be taken as
69:1921:137689:15:15:90:504:155:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:definitive; if different methods were adopted it would be possible for a different
69:1922:137771:15:15:90:504:140:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:range of results to be produced. The methodological approaches developed in this
69:1923:137851:15:15:90:504:125:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:paper are innovative and, as the nature of this paper should be seen as consultative,
69:1924:137936:15:0:90:339:110:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:we welcome other views on the issues presented.
70:1925:138042:0:38:90:220:562:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:Appendix
70:1926:138050:38:39:90:499:524:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:Savings and investment within
70:1927:138079:39:39:90:186:485:1024:g_d0_f7:1024:g_d0_f7:NiGEM
70:1928:138084:39:15:90:504:446:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:For the scenarios we analyse here, the description within NiGEM of household sector
70:1929:138167:15:15:90:504:431:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:savings and of national savings and investment deserves some comment. Households
70:1930:138247:15:15:90:504:416:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:receive  income  from  employment,  transfer  income  from  the  public  sector,  and
70:1931:138332:15:15:90:504:401:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income from households’ net financial assets. Households’ financial assets include
70:1932:138414:15:15:90:504:386:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assets held overseas, government debt, deposits held in monetary institutions and
70:1933:138495:15:15:90:504:371:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:equity holdings. Of that income households pay tax, consume and save. In the long
70:1934:138576:15:15:90:504:356:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:run the household savings ratio, i.e. the share of households’ disposable income
70:1935:138656:15:15:90:504:341:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:that is not consumed, is determined by the ratio of household wealth to income.
70:1936:138735:15:15:90:504:326:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Household wealth includes financial assets less financial liabilities, the majority of
70:1937:138821:15:15:90:504:311:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:which is mortgage debt, and housing wealth. In the short run the savings ratio is
70:1938:138902:15:15:90:504:296:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:affected by different dynamics between consumption expenditure, the two wealth
70:1939:138980:15:15:90:504:281:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:components  and  disposable  income.  The  estimated  equation  for  household
70:1940:139058:15:15:90:504:266:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption, embodying the long run savings ratio described here, is reported in
70:1941:139138:15:15:90:504:251:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Barrell et al. (2003), and in most scenarios we utilise the assumption that individuals
70:1942:139225:15:15:90:504:236:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:form  (correct)  expectations  about  their  future  incomes  when  making  their
70:1943:139306:15:25:90:381:221:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:consumption decisions in relation to ‘permanent income’.
70:1944:139362:25:15:90:504:196:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:By identity a change in household sector savings must be mirrored in a change in
70:1945:139442:15:15:90:504:181:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:investment  either  at  home  or  abroad,  unless  it  is  associated  with  an  offsetting
70:1946:139533:15:15:90:504:166:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:change  in  saving  elsewhere  in  the  economy.  Within  NiGEM  three  categories  of
70:1947:139619:15:15:90:504:151:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:domestic investment are modelled separately. The company sector invests in capital
70:1948:139701:15:15:90:504:136:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:so that in the long run the marginal rate of return to capital equals its real user cost.
70:1949:139790:15:15:90:504:121:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:The underlying production function is CES (constant elasticity of substitution) and
70:1950:139873:15:15:90:504:106:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:this means that it is the capital-output ratio that is determined by the real user cost
70:1951:139960:15:15:90:504:91:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of capital. Government investment is determined by policy in the short run. In the
70:1952:140042:15:15:90:504:76:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:longer term, all else equal, it is expected to grow in relation to needs reflected in the
70:1953:140131:15:15:90:504:61:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:age structure of the population. Housing investment rises with household sector
70:1954:140210:15:0:90:470:46:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:personal incomes and is reduced by a rise in the long-term real interest rate.
71:1955:140288:0:106:16:29:821:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:62
71:1956:140337:106:15:90:504:715:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:Government saving is determined by tax revenues less public sector expenditures,
71:1957:140417:15:15:90:504:700:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:and these are determined endogenously within NiGEM, with targets set for the level
71:1958:140499:15:15:90:504:685:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:of government borrowing. Company sector savings are determined as the residual
71:1959:140577:15:15:90:504:670:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:category of the savings-investment identity. The excess of investment over saving for
71:1960:140662:15:15:90:504:655:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:the UK economy as a whole is represented by the current account deficit of the
71:1961:140740:15:15:90:504:640:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:balance of payments. Within NiGEM competitiveness, export and import demand
71:1962:140815:15:15:90:504:625:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:are  all  endogenously  determined  and  reflect  trade  with  a  broad  range  of  other
71:1963:140904:15:15:90:504:610:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:economies. Income derived from net foreign assets held abroad, or net property
71:1964:140982:15:15:90:504:595:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:income, is determined by rates of return on assets held abroad and on foreign held
71:1965:141064:15:15:90:504:580:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:assets in the UK. Net foreign assets reflect the cumulated surpluses on the current
71:1966:141147:15:5:90:134:565:144:g_d0_f7:144:g_d0_f7:account.
